Current Commentary

Opinions on Improving News Censorship 24

— Du

Guaranteeing the voice of public opinion has been repeatedly shouted in our ears. Grand proposals and eloquent debates have never failed to be inspiring and desirable, causing us to look forward to their realization. Most recently, at the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee, Zhou Fohai and 55 others proposed that the National Government issue a national order to effectively guarantee public opinion and that the Standing Committee effectively improve news censorship measures. The proposal was resolved and passed by the Third Congress. Observing that the word "effective" has been repeatedly invoked this time, it seems that this is not to be compared with the usual empty words. After this national order is issued by the National Government, if local agencies still engage in destroying legitimate public opinion, they will be treating laws like old shoes and disregarding the Central Government. For the sake of safeguarding national prestige, the Central Government must implement appropriate sanctions to annotate the word "effective." How should we, who are engaged in the news business, improve our mind and body and do our best to fulfill our responsibilities, to represent the voice of the people and live up to the expectations of the country? As for news censorship, it was originally a temporary measure. Before the turbulent situation has been completely stabilized, the government does not want to abolish it hastily, and we should show sympathy and understanding. However, the urgent need to improve censorship measures is a reality that cannot be ignored. Now, before the Standing Committee has drafted a new system, I would like to express my opinions.

The motivation for censoring news is originally to facilitate administration. On the one hand, it is used to prevent the leakage of confidential information, and on the other hand, it is also to clarify the authorities' position in handling affairs. Therefore, its target is entirely the interests of the country. It is, in fact, a kind of unavoidable measure in extraordinary times. In the past, news censorship seemed to have failed to fully satisfy people's expectations. Regarding the points to be improved in the future, I believe that, first, the scope and standards of censorship should be determined. Military strategies and diplomatic policies are related to the party and the country's major plans and should not be disclosed arbitrarily. They should be included in the scope of censorship. Other similar events that the government considers necessary to keep secret, but cannot list one by one, may have standards set to follow. As for local facilities, private gains and losses, and trivial issues that are irrelevant to the overall direction, they should not be restricted by using one's authority, to comply with the purpose of protecting public opinion. Second, the qualifications of censors should be clearly defined, and they should be given the power to respond flexibly. Censors should be obligated to obey their superiors and responsible for upholding newspapers. When uncertain events occur, and the scope and standards are unclear, censors must use their clear minds, make a balanced observation, use common sense to judge, and meet practical needs. If the authorities can give censors the flexibility to respond in advance and not nitpick afterwards, then censors and newspapers can maintain a spirit of coordination and avoid unnecessary disputes. Otherwise, when censors encounter questionable issues, they lack the power to release them after weighing the circumstances, and they are not allowed time to consult their superiors. They will inevitably resort to arbitrary deletion to avoid responsibility to their superiors. Such a lack of standards will lead to disorder. Often, news of the same nature is either correct yesterday but wrong today, or released here but withheld there. Some are cut off as soon as they appear, while others arrive unexpectedly without explaining the cause. Readers are confused, and newspapers are blamed. All of this is difficult to deny in reality. I sincerely hope that the committee members of the Standing Committee will make effective improvements in the new regulations.

Three Japanese Arrive in Xuzhou for Inspection 25

(Xuzhou) The Japan International Tourist Bureau has dispatched a group of three, namely Tanaka Seijiro, Kanai Seikei, and Hojo Yasuhei, to inspect the Pinghan and Longhai railway lines. They arrived in Xuzhou this morning from Zhengzhou and visited various places in the city. They are scheduled to go to Lianyungang for inspection on the 9th before returning to Tianjin. (8th Dispatch from Central News Agency)

The Most Important International Gathering Since the War: Naval Conference Opens This Morning 26

How to Remedy the Damaged Naval Treaty? 27

Success or Failure Hinges on Japan's Attitude 28

Conference Will Inevitably Involve Far Eastern Political Issues 29

(London) Today, a group of carpenters and electricians left the famous "Locarno Room" of the Foreign Office, a sign that all preparations for the most important international gathering since the war, the Naval Conference, which opens tomorrow, are complete. The conference will take place behind the scenes at Clarence House, located in Westminster, along the River Thames. The duration of the conference cannot be predicted at present, but it is expected to last about six weeks. (Reuters, 8th)

(London) The Naval Conference will open on Monday. The shattered Washington Treaty, as it stands today, seems impossible to salvage. A naval arms race, costing world powers countless sums of money and driven by a surge of nationalism, also appears inevitable. According to the provisions of the Washington Treaty, a conference must be convened one year after any signatory nation announces its withdrawal. Now, as Britain issues its invitations, the situation caused by the Italian-Ethiopian War is exerting great pressure, and the Far East is facing a serious crisis due to the issue of autonomy in North China. British and American authorities have expressed deep concern, stating that the Nine-Power Treaty and the Naval Treaty are related, and any violations will not be tolerated. However, after the Naval Conference opens, even if Japan's demand for equality can overcome British and American opposition and be satisfied, the antagonism between France and Italy will still require careful consideration. The Anglo-German Naval Agreement has effectively nullified the naval clauses of the Treaty of Versailles. France will naturally need to increase its naval strength. Therefore, experienced observers here generally believe that this conference is completely hopeless for reducing armaments, and even hopes of preventing expansion are slim. (National Telegraph, 7th)

Locarno Room Newly Decorated

(London) The Naval Conference is scheduled to formally open at the Foreign Office's "Locarno Room" at noon on Monday, chaired by Prime Minister Baldwin. This room, located on the second floor of the Foreign Office, is where the Locarno Treaties were signed. The room is rectangular, spacious, and has many windows. The walls are adorned with red brocade, and long tables covered in green felt are placed along the walls for the conference's use. Looking out of the windows, one sees the courtyard of the Foreign Office. Only a small number of journalists will be allowed into the conference venue during the opening session, but they will not be allowed to leave during the conference. Other journalists will wait in the nearby Foreign Office restaurant. Speeches from the conference will be transmitted to the next room via microphones, and the full text of the speeches will be recorded by stenographers. All documents will be distributed to the press by the conference secretariat. The planned program is for Prime Minister Baldwin to deliver the opening address first, followed by the chief representatives of each country speaking in alphabetical order by country name. Regarding the language to be used at the conference, Britain proposes that only English be used as the official language. However, due to objections raised by the French representatives, the secretariat has decided that all speeches and documents will be in both English and French, with translators from the Foreign Office providing translation services. Subsequent meetings will be held at "Clarence House," across from the Foreign Office. The British government has rented two floors specifically for the conference. (Havas, 7th)

The Formation of Opposition Between Britain, America, and Japan

(London) The characteristic of this conference is that the participating countries have not agreed on a common stance beforehand. According to unofficial observations, this matter is as difficult to untangle as tangled silk, and its success largely depends on Japan's attitude. Japan is now firmly demanding that its navy be equal to those of Britain and America, which is the most significant obstacle to the conference. If Japan can achieve this, it is willing to abolish or greatly limit battleships, aircraft carriers, and 10,000-ton cruisers. Britain, due to the need to defend its global empire, opposes equality with Japan. However, it may welcome smaller battleships and cruisers, with a tonnage limit of 7,000 tons. But Britain's current recognition of the 50-cruiser limit is only temporary, and it will eventually restore the old limit of at least 70 cruisers. Britain will also likely advocate extending the age of battleships from 20 years to 26 years, which is expected to be one of the points for achieving a general compromise. The United States also firmly opposes Japan's demand for equality and wants to maintain the warship types previously agreed upon in Washington, i.e., battleships limited to 35,000 tons and cruisers limited to 10,000 tons. The United States may agree to reduce the caliber of battleship guns from 16 inches. It is reported that the United States also wants to have the same number of cruisers as Britain but may agree to the abolition of submarines. The US and Japanese delegations have not been authorized by their governments to handle political issues. However, the United States is deeply concerned about the North China situation, so Japan's China policy being brought into the conference is also on everyone's mind. (Reuters, 8th)

Franco-Italian Amity Makes Compromise Easier

(London) Britain and France have had friendly diplomatic contacts in recent days, so France is closely harmonized with Britain on several points. However, France is unwilling to make any commitments until it better understands Germany's intentions. Furthermore, France is unwilling to agree to the abolition of submarines. Italy previously demanded the same number of submarines as France, which greatly angered France. However, the recent friendship between the two countries may make this easier to compromise. Italy currently has 83 submarines, most of which are very new, so it is determined not to abolish this weapon. Furthermore, Italy has already begun building two 35,000-ton battleships, which is causing Britain great concern in the Mediterranean. (Reuters, 8th)

Anglo-Japanese Preliminary Talks: Japan Insists on Equal Demands 30

(London) The naval conference representatives of Britain and Japan held preliminary talks today, mainly discussing conference preparation issues. The representatives of France, Italy, and the United States are scheduled to officially visit the Navy Department tomorrow. (National Telegraph, 7th)

(London) Plenipotentiaries Nagano and Nagai, along with Chief Commissioner Iwashita, visited the British Navy Department at 10:30 AM on the 7th, conducting discussions in the form of inquiries. The British representatives also raised various questions during the meeting. Plenipotentiary Nagano clarified Japan's policy as follows:

(1) A common maximum limit must be set for the naval strength maintained by each country, establishing substantive equality of naval power. (2) The British government's proposed shipbuilding notification plan cannot be approved unless it is based on the above principle. (3) Regarding submarines, the necessary quantity for self-determination is absolutely required based on national defense needs. (United Press, 7th)

Main Points of Japanese Representative's Speech: Principles of Non-Threat and Non-Aggression 31

(Tokyo) The 9th is the first day of the Disarmament Conference. The Japanese delegation will exchange greetings with the representatives of various countries. Then, Plenipotentiary Nagano will clearly state the fundamental principles of Japan, the gist of which is roughly as follows:

(1) World peace is an indispensable requirement for national survival. The Japanese government is greatly concerned about promoting the realization of disarmament efforts to ensure international peace. It has always cooperated with related countries at disarmament conferences and has worked to promote the success of disarmament endeavors. (2) The Japanese government, in discussing the reduction of naval armaments, is always based on the spirit of disarmament, striving not to harm the sense of security of various countries, fully considering the geographical position and special circumstances of each country, in order to reach fair and reasonable solutions based on the actual situation. It hopes that this will become the guiding principle of future conferences. (3) The Japanese government believes that the leveling of armaments is the most practical method that should be implemented at this time. (4) Regarding naval power, the Japanese government believes that a maximum limit that can be recognized by all countries should be set. Within that limit, each country should exercise autonomous armament based on defensive and geographical positions, in order to realize the principle of non-threat and non-aggression. Therefore, it first requests the implementation of a common maximum limit agreement, followed by the signing of a concrete treaty on armaments. (United Press, 8th)

Navy Minister Osumi Issues Statement 32

(Tokyo) The London Naval Conference will open on the 9th. Navy Minister Osumi issued a statement in the form of a discussion regarding Japan's determination to attend this conference, as follows: According to the provisions of the Washington and London treaties, the Naval Disarmament Conference is scheduled to open in London on the 9th. Representatives from Japan, Britain, the United States, France, and Italy will attend. Japan's fundamental policy for attending this conference has been repeatedly clarified to both domestic and foreign audiences since the preliminary negotiations last year. It advocates establishing a common maximum limit for the amount of naval power that may not be exceeded among major navies, while thoroughly implementing disarmament to establish the principle of non-threat and non-aggression among countries, in order to contribute to the permanent peace and prosperity of the world. The arguments of the other participating countries are different, so the future of the negotiations is difficult to predict. However, it is believed that the ultimate goals of world peace and prosperity are the same. If this common ultimate goal is not taken lightly and unreasonable sentiments are put aside, and sincere and open discussions are conducted together, then the best solution to the problem will undoubtedly converge on what Japan advocates. This disarmament conference is of great significance to Japan in light of internal and external situations. Therefore, we should unite as a country, ensure the future national defense of the country, and look forward to the true peace of the world and the happiness of all mankind. (United Press, 8th)

US and Japan Form Confrontational Stance 33

(London) According to reliable sources close to US Chief Representative Davis, the United States will consistently oppose Japan's demand for equal rights. It is generally believed that the confrontational state between the US and Japan will be clearly exposed once the Naval Conference officially opens on Monday. The hope of discussing naval issues under the quantitative restriction format adopted by the Washington and London Naval Treaties will inevitably be abandoned. Regarding this confrontational state, it is rumored that the Japanese delegation will refuse to discuss naval issues under narrower technical issues. However, this statement was denied by the Japanese delegation last night. (Havas, 8th)

Attending Senate Today: Italian Prime Minister to Deliver Speech 34

(Rome) It is reported that Prime Minister Mussolini will deliver a speech in the Senate tomorrow, commenting on the talks recently held in Paris by the representatives of Britain and France. (Havas, 8th)

Nine-Power Treaty: The Balance of Power in the Far East Depends on It 35

Has a Related Relationship with the Naval Treaty 36

The United States Believes There Is Absolutely No Reason to Amend It 37

(Washington) Government leaders remain very cold today toward the semi-official Japanese suggestion that the signatories of the Nine-Power Treaty should find ways to revise the treaty. They have expressed in their personal capacities that there is no reason to amend the treaty, and they believe that even after revision, it cannot change the actual situation in China. It would only legalize Japan's actions and intentions in Manchuria and North China, which are currently considered here to be violations of the treaty and other related treaties regarding China. Some believe that the remarks of the Japanese Foreign Ministry's spokesman show that Japanese leaders are gradually feeling the pressure from Britain and the United States. In addition, the League of Nations' attitude toward Italy's breach of treaty is becoming increasingly tough. Secretary of State Hull's statement, requesting that other signatory nations jointly assert their rights and demand compliance with all treaties, is considered here to be a direct action that aroused the interest of various countries in the Far Eastern situation, so that the League of Nations can also pay attention to Japan. Authoritative sources claim that without the Nine-Power Treaty and the Four-Power Treaty, naval disarmament cannot proceed. The implication is that if the Nine-Power Treaty is revised, it will disrupt the political balance of power in the Far East, and naval disarmament will become even more impossible. (National Telegraph, 7th)

British and French Giants Hold Diplomatic Talks in Paris: 38

Suggestions to Resolve the Italian-Ethiopian Dispute are Adjusted 39

Naval Cooperation in the Mediterranean is Also Touched Upon 40

Italian Prime Minister's Attitude is Stubborn, and Hopes for Peace are Slim 41

(London) Last night, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's strong speech in the Chamber of Deputies dashed all hopes of an early resolution to the Italian-Ethiopian War. Geneva views the future as extremely bleak because Mussolini has refused to negotiate. British Foreign Secretary Hoare will confer with French Prime Minister Laval multiple times in Paris today to determine future steps, so the eyes of the general public are now focused on Paris. The first meeting between the two key officials was held last night at the French Foreign Ministry, lasting two hours and fifteen minutes. British Foreign Office experts on African affairs, Peterson, British Ambassador to France, Clerk, and British Undersecretary of State Vansittart were all in attendance. After the meeting, Laval issued a communiqué stating that the British and French governments are in complete agreement on their mutual objectives and close cooperation. The meeting will continue tomorrow morning at 10:30 AM. (Reuters, 8th)

(Paris) British and French talks continued at the Foreign Ministry this morning at 10:30, ending at 12:20 noon. Those present on the British side were Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare, Under-Secretary of State Sir Robert Vansittart, Ambassador to France Sir George Clerk, and Abyssinian affairs expert Mr. Peterson. The French side was represented by Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Pierre Laval, Secretary-General of the Foreign Ministry Alexis Léger, and Director of African Affairs Saint-Quentin. According to our correspondent, the future progress of the Italian-Ethiopian issue will depend on Italy's attitude. The nature of this morning's talks was largely technical. The intention was to adjust the suggestions drafted by Saint-Quentin and Peterson to draft a substantive proposal. Once drafted, it should be submitted to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, and approximately simultaneously sent to the League of Nations and the Ethiopian Emperor. Our correspondent also learned that the British and French will invite Aloisi, chief of staff of the Italian Prime Minister's Office, to bring Mussolini's reply to Paris, or directly to Geneva, so that continued negotiations can be conducted as soon as possible. Regardless of the negotiation situation, the Committee of Eighteen will still meet as scheduled on the 12th of this month. The British and French governments will submit a report on the results of their mediation of the dispute, so that the oil embargo can be postponed if necessary. After this morning's talks concluded, the British representatives stayed for lunch with Laval. Discussions will continue in the afternoon. (Havas, 8th)

(Paris) According to our diplomatic correspondent, if the British and French talks cannot reach a complete compromise tonight, British Foreign Secretary Hoare may stay here one more day and will not depart for St. Moritz, Switzerland, tomorrow. Future talks will likely be conducted by British Undersecretary of State Vansittart and French Secretary-General of the Foreign Ministry Léger, along with experts from both countries, to complete the draft proposal. (Havas, 8th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations deeply feels that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's speech in the Chamber of Deputies has completely cut off the hope of peace before the end of this year. It is believed here today that although the League of Nations threatens to pass oil and coal-iron sanctions, Italy will still go its own way. British Foreign Secretary Hoare's speech last Thursday also indicated that Britain will continue to support the League of Nations. Therefore, the Committee of Eighteen's passage of a proposal to implement an oil embargo and copper, coal, and iron sanctions against Italy as soon as possible is now unavoidable. (National Telegraph, 7th)

British-French Talks Range Widely

(Paris) According to our correspondent, during the Hoare-Laval talks yesterday, in addition to the Italian-Ethiopian issue, the following were also discussed: (1) Relations between Britain and France and Germany; (2) the Air Locarno Pact; and (3) the problem of cooperation between Britain and France in the Mediterranean. Massigli from the French Foreign Ministry on disarmament issues was also present. Regarding items one and two, Hoare and Laval re-examined the various proposals recommended in the Anglo-French London Declaration of February 3 of this year. (These proposals were: (A) Concluding a convention to limit armaments to replace the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles; (B) Germany rejoining the League of Nations; (C) Signing the Air Pact; (D) Signing the Danube Pact; (E) Signing the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact) and re-agreed on concluding the Air Pact and limiting air force armaments. However, because Germany insists on resolving the Italian-Ethiopian dispute before discussing the above issues, it is unknown whether Britain and France will re-submit the negotiations to Berlin. Regarding the third item, Mediterranean cooperation, Hoare and Laval decided that experts from both countries should immediately hold talks to discuss it. As for the Italian-Ethiopian dispute, according to our correspondent, Britain is now prepared to make some concessions. For example, the country previously advocated that Ethiopia should cede its southern land to Italy, up to 40 degrees east longitude, and now it is willing to extend it to 38 degrees east longitude according to the French proposal. However, there are still a number of difficult points that remain to be resolved, so it is difficult to predict when the British and French talks will have a real effect. (Havas, 8th)

High Pressure Will Be Applied to Italy

(Paris) British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister Laval held meetings all day today. At the same time, it is learned that Britain and France have exerted significant pressure on Italy. The French Foreign Ministry telegraphed new instructions to the French Ambassador to Italy, Chambrun, ordering him to convey them to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. It is also learned that after the British Ambassador to Italy met with Mussolini, he also met with Italian Undersecretary of State Suvich. (National Telegraph, 7th)

(London) According to well-informed sources in Paris, Hoare and Laval have resolved that the two countries should jointly send a note to the Italian government. If Mussolini's reply does not satisfy the two countries, then the two countries should advocate in the Committee of Eighteen's meeting on December 12 that an oil embargo against Italy should be implemented from January 1 of next year. This procedure gives Italy room to maneuver, allowing it to change its views before the new year. (Reuters, 8th)

Implementation of the Oil Embargo Cannot Be Delayed

(London) It is heard that some parties in Geneva do not consider delaying the decision to implement the oil embargo to be appropriate. Although this view is not supported by the majority, the repeated bombing of undefended towns in Ethiopia by Italian aircraft has made all parties feel that implementing the oil embargo is an urgent matter. British Minister for League of Nations Affairs, Eden, is scheduled to go to Geneva within this week to participate in the important meeting of the Committee of Eighteen. Mussolini's speech, though it may be said to have not completely closed the door to negotiations, in reality does not want to seek a solution to the dispute, so both London and Paris view it as stubborn. The British and French governments are still determined to proceed with everything according to the peace plan set by the experts of the two countries in Paris. (Reuters, 8th)

Cession of Territory Is Not Acceptable to Ethiopia

(London) It is heard that the suggestions of the experts of Britain and France do not satisfy Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's request for the connection between Illyria and Somaliland. According to this request, if it is to be realized, it will be necessary to cede Ethiopia's Harar province to Italy. The Ethiopian Emperor has already notified Britain and France that this is not acceptable. (Havas, 7th)

Page 6

Disappointment Over Italian Prime Minister's Strong Rhetoric: 42

The Prospect of Peace Talks Is Bleak 43

(Paris) Although the French Foreign Ministry is not making any statements about Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's speech in the Chamber of Deputies today, they all believe that Mussolini's speech has caused disappointment on all sides. The reason is that Mussolini not only did not specify the minimum demands that Italy intends to make on Ethiopia, but on the contrary, reiterated that if Italy's rights and interests in Africa are not recognized, it will continue military action until it achieves final victory. Therefore, even if British Foreign Secretary Hoare and French Prime Minister Laval have reached an agreement in today's meeting, the prospects for peace talks are very bleak. (Havas, 7th)

(London) According to well-informed sources here, a pessimistic impression was formed when news came from Rome earlier that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini had no intention of negotiating peace at the time. Now, judging from Mussolini's speech in the Chamber of Deputies today, this statement has been confirmed. Therefore, it is believed that the method of embargoing coal and oil will be implemented when the Committee of Eighteen meets on the 12th of this month. But there are those who say that Mussolini's public mention of attempts at conciliation on all sides is actually the first time. From this, it can be seen that diplomatic negotiations are not without the possibility of success. (Havas, 7th)

(Rome) Mussolini's speech in the Chamber of Deputies yesterday was very short, which was quite unexpected. His speech was warmly cheered by the entire chamber. After the speech, the parliament adjourned until next Tuesday. Mussolini said: "We have reached the 365th day, and we still hold the same aspirations, the same courage, and the same determination as on the first day." Next, he referred to the peace request recently made to him by British Ambassador to Rome, Sir Drummond, saying: "In these recent hours, the atmosphere seems to have improved slightly, but I must warn you not to be too optimistic too early." He then referred to British Foreign Secretary Hoare's statement in the House of Commons on Thursday that he wanted to see a strong Italy, saying that this fact is impossible if the entire security of East Africa and the colonies is not resolved. He went on to say: "The oil embargo, which will be discussed on December 12, will seriously hinder the overall situation. The League of Nations has never implemented sanctions for events that are far more serious than the Ethiopian case. The only reason why it is being implemented against Italy is because Italy is poor in raw materials." Finally, he made a firm statement that the dispute could only be resolved after the rights and the protection of Italian interests it should enjoy in Africa were clearly recognized. After Mussolini finished speaking, the entire chamber cheered for three minutes, followed by singing the national anthem. (Reuters, 8th)

Italian Senate Supports Mussolini's Policy 44

(Rome) The government issued a substitute legal decree on August 23, ordering the Ministry of Finance to raise extraordinary expenses for use in East Africa. The Senate is scheduled to meet tomorrow, and the agenda includes the approval of the aforementioned substitute legal decree. It is generally expected that the Senate's enthusiastic support for Prime Minister Mussolini's policies will not be less than that of the Chamber of Deputies. In addition, a majority of senators, including wireless inventor Marconi and several members of the royal family, jointly submitted a motion that will be defended by Finance Minister Thaon di Revel. This motion states in brief: "The Royal Italian Senate, now united with the national people, unites to resist the most unjust and absurd attempt to reduce Italy's aspirations (referring to sanctions), and reiterates that Italy's actions in East Africa are entirely a legitimate act of self-defense and contain the profound meaning of instilling culture in Africa. This has been solemnly explained by our King Victor Emmanuel III. The Senate declares that it is united with the actions of Prime Minister Mussolini and firmly believes that the Prime Minister will not fail to fulfill his duty to preserve Italy's honor and rights." (Havas, 8th)

Economic Sanctions to End War: Majority of US Congressmen Express Support 45

(Washington) The Associated Press today sought opinions from members of the Senate and the House of Representatives and has learned that eight out of ten are in favor of using economic sanctions to stop the war. Their answers have indicated that Congress will pass embargoes on oil, cotton, and other goods, and they have said that if such actions are necessary for the United States to maintain neutrality, then the people they represent will do their utmost to advocate neutrality. (National Telegraph, 7th)

Italian Planes Fly Over Taixi, Intensify Fierce Bombing, Rain of Incendiary Bombs, A's Army Camp Destroyed 46

Fifty Meters Around Engulfed in Flames

Taigeli Province Frontline: Our correspondent Ba'er reports that a squadron of Italian Air Force planes flew to Taixi City and dropped bombs on the camps of thousands of A's troops stationed there. This type of target is fixed and easy to hit. According to initial reports, all the camps were destroyed by the bombing, and the city also suffered significant damage. The bombs dropped were incendiary in nature, and everything within a 50-meter radius of the impact point immediately caught fire. (Rome) Military experts observe that the Italian Air Force's bombing of Taixi City can be described as the most arduous operation in the history of aerial warfare. Eighteen planes participated in the bombing, traveling a round trip distance of 900 kilometers. Taixi City is extremely high in altitude, 2,640 meters above sea level, surrounded by plateaus of about 3,000 meters. The A's have placed numerous anti-aircraft defense installations in all important locations, and the defending personnel are all trained by European officers. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

(London) According to reports from A Capital, no fewer than eighty people were killed and no fewer than two hundred wounded in the Italian plane's bombing of Taixi on Friday. Many of the wounded have little hope of survival. Yesterday, Italian planes attacked Taixi again, dropping 50 bombs, but there were no casualties because most residents had fled into the mountains. At the same time, the Italian Embassy here, after receiving news from Rome, issued a statement denying the claim that an American hospital in Taixi or Gondar was destroyed by Italian planes yesterday. It also stated that the use of incendiary bombs by Italian planes was in retaliation for the A soldiers' use of Temtem gun bullets. A Capital: Our special correspondent stationed in Taixi City, Gao Yixiong, was also affected by the Italian planes' large-scale bombing of Taixi City yesterday. Gao Yixiong has now been transported to the capital by plane for treatment. His account of the Italian planes' bombing and the heroic resistance of the A soldiers and civilians is very detailed, and is specially supplemented as follows: It is said that yesterday morning, four Italian bombers first flew over Taixi City and circled for several minutes before dropping several 100-kilogram bombs, hitting the city market, killing seven people. Subsequently, several incendiary bombs were dropped, and many houses immediately caught fire upon impact. Finally, they flew back and forth over the tents of the American hospital, ultimately incinerating them with bombs. Fortunately, the patients in the hospital had been evacuated in time. Only one Swedish nurse, in a moment of panic, jumped out of a window and suffered serious injuries to her legs. At that time, fires broke out everywhere in the city, and shouts echoed. Although Italian planes dropped several bombs on the A Emperor's residence, the damage was not severe. Soon after, sixteen more Italian planes sped in, and the 100-kilogram bombs they dropped mostly landed on the ground more than 100 meters away from the American hospital. At that time, the A troops immediately met the enemy with rifles, machine guns, and anti-aircraft guns, while the police fired pistols into the air, firing an estimated 20,000 rounds of bullets. One Italian plane appeared to have been hit, but it was still able to fly away quickly along with the other Italian planes. In total, the Italian planes bombed twice, lasting one hour. As of midnight yesterday, the number of people killed had reached as many as 50, of which only three were soldiers. Most of the deceased did not die immediately, but succumbed to their injuries. Many more are currently seriously injured, and their fate is difficult to predict. The A people, after the disaster, were able to endure the pain and support each other. Their spirit is truly admirable. After the Italian planes flew away yesterday morning, the city's journalists, together with police and nurses, went to visit the affected people. (Havas dispatch, 7th)

Overseas Chinese Wang Zhenshan Invents a Carburetor Car: Uses Sulat Oil Instead of Petrol, British Government Grants Five-Year Patent 51

China Union News Agency, Singapore: Wang Zhenshan, the owner of the Wang Zhenshan Automobile Company on Juche Road, Singapore, a native of Fuqing, Fujian Province, came to the south at a young age to study machinery, and is particularly skilled in automobile technology research. He recently invented a carburetor car that can use Sulat oil (i.e., the residue left over from refining kerosene) instead of petrol. It has been approved by the British government's four state vehicle affairs department as a qualified long-distance passenger car, and has been granted a five-year patent. According to Mr. Wang's interview with reporters, replacing petrol with Sulat oil in the carburetor car is six cents cheaper per gallon and can travel eight miles further. The carburetor car can certainly also run on kerosene or alcohol. He also said that in recent years, roads have been opened up in our country, and there are many cars, and the required petrol is mostly imported, causing a shocking outflow of wealth. If carburetor cars are used and domestic Sulat oil, alcohol, or kerosene is used instead of petrol, the outflow of wealth can be avoided, and there is no fear of supply disruption. He is now planning to raise funds to return to China to set up a factory to manufacture carburetor cars, which would benefit both the country and himself.

Economic Essays 75

— Edited by Tang Qing

Labor-Capital Coordination - Zhu Tongjiu

I. The Significance of Labor-Capital Coordination After the Industrial Revolution, labor and capital formed a confrontational situation, with open strife and covert struggles, each doing their best. Today, workers strike, and tomorrow, employers shut down factories, each using their combat tools to do their best to defeat the enemy. In fact, labor and capital are both indispensable elements in production, and should cooperate with each other to increase production and benefit society. Now, they misunderstand each other and recklessly engage in strife, which not only causes huge losses to both labor and capital, but also leads to low production, social unrest, and a serious impact on the overall welfare of society. Governments of various countries, in view of this, have promulgated laws stipulating that both labor and capital shall not arbitrarily strike or shut down factories. If there are disagreements or conflicts of interest, they must follow the prescribed legal procedures to engage in mediation; if mediation fails, arbitration shall follow to prevent the matter from escalating and to resolve it as soon as possible. This kind of mediation or arbitration is called labor-capital coordination.

II. Causes of Labor Disputes The causes of labor disputes are numerous and vary with changes in social circumstances. However, the main reasons are nothing more than increasing wages and improving treatment. In 1926, there were 535 strikes, of which 250 were due to economic oppression, accounting for 46.7% of the total; 172 were due to treatment issues, accounting for approximately 31.1% of the total. According to the 1929 Shanghai strike statistics, there were 111 strikes, of which 36 were due to employment and dismissal issues, accounting for 32.43% of the total, ranking first. 26 strikes were due to wage issues, accounting for 23.43% of the total, ranking second. In 1933, the total number of labor disputes in China was 527. 167 were due to dismissal or employment relationships, accounting for 31.69% of the total; 127 were due to wage issues, accounting for 24.10% of the total. According to the above statistics, it can be seen that there are two main reasons for labor disputes: one is dismissal or employment relationship, and the other is wage issues. As for other reasons, according to the 1935 supplement to the Chinese Economic Yearbook, they are roughly as follows: A. Labor disputes related to negotiations with organizations, (1) coordination aspects of labor unions and workers, a. work, b. labor agreements. (2) Those related to employment conditions, including a. wages, b. working hours, c. treatment, d. factory rules, e. work system, f. employment or dismissal, g. shutdown or temporary shutdown. B. Labor disputes unrelated to negotiations with organizations, (1) sympathetic, (2) political, (3) other.

III. Principles of Labor-Capital Coordination The purpose of labor-capital coordination is to maintain industrial peace, and in order to make labor-capital coordination effective, the principles of labor-capital coordination must first be determined in order to proceed smoothly and for both labor and capital to comply willingly. The principles of labor coordination are approximately as follows:

1. Strictly Stipulate Employment and Dismissal Methods An investigation of the primary cause of labor disputes in my country in recent years is the issue of employment or dismissal. Therefore, in order to avoid the occurrence of disputes, the conditions for employment and dismissal must be strictly defined. When factories employ workers on a regular basis, workers cannot be arbitrarily dismissed if they are without fault. At the same time, if dismissal is unavoidable, workers must be notified in advance so that they can look for work in a calm manner as soon as possible, without suffering the pain of immediate unemployment. Moreover, factories must pay severance pay when dismissing workers, which is the so-called DismissalWays. After such strict regulations, factories must be cautious about dismissing workers, otherwise they will inevitably suffer the loss of paying severance pay. Therefore, in order to avoid losses and reduce the mobility of skilled workers, factories will inevitably be unwilling to dismiss workers at will, and disputes can be reduced. Moreover, if a third party or the government comes forward to mediate or arbitrate, there will be a basis for reference, and disputes can easily be concluded in a short period of time.

2. Wages and Living Standards The second main cause of labor disputes is the wage issue. Therefore, the level of wages or whether to increase them should be based on the standard of living. If the price level rises and the purchasing power of money wages declines, then factories should increase money wages. Therefore, if a dispute arises due to a wage issue, the increase in wages should be based on the degree of increase in prices, so that the wages earned by workers can purchase the food necessary for life, to meet the minimum material requirements of the workers. Moreover, whether the workers' food is sufficient is closely related to the workers' work efficiency. If workers eat too little nutrition, work efficiency will decrease, resulting in intangible losses for the factory. Therefore, the determination of the amount of wages must be based on the standard of living.

3. Public Enterprises Public enterprises such as tap water, electricity, telephone, trams, buses, railways, post offices, etc., do not aim to make profits, but to serve society. Moreover, the operation of the above-mentioned public enterprises is now mostly handled by the government or local public agencies, so the object of public enterprise workers is the public or the government. Therefore, workers in public enterprises, no matter how poor their treatment or how reduced their wages, cannot immediately announce a strike if their demands are not met. Because the suspension of such public enterprises is to the detriment of society as a whole. Therefore, various countries have promulgated strict regulations for workers in public enterprises. If they have reasonable demands, they must comply with certain procedures, apply according to law, and wait for the authorities to approve and handle them. Strikes, on the other hand, are absolutely prohibited. Article 4 of my country's Labor Dispute Resolution Law stipulates: "If a labor dispute occurs in the following undertakings, and the matter has been mediated without result, it shall be submitted to the Arbitration Committee for arbitration. (1) Tap water, electric light, or gas undertakings for public needs. (2) Postal, telegraph, telephone, railway, tram, shipping, and public bus undertakings for public needs." The so-called arbitration means that after the ruling of the Arbitration Committee, both labor and capital shall not declare any objections, which implies compulsory execution and prohibition. Therefore, Article 7 of the same law stipulates that "The parties to the dispute shall not declare dissatisfaction with the judgment of the Arbitration Committee."

Floodwaters in Hanchuan Haven't Receded 77

More Than 700,000 Mu of Fertile Land Still Submerged - The Cao River and Gao Xiang River Urgently Need Dredging

Hankou Correspondence: This year's floods in Hubei Province are most severe in the Xiang River basin, affecting Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan counties. The floodwaters have not receded since summer, and the suffering of the disaster victims exceeds all previous records. Meng Guangpeng, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs and Chairman of the Disaster Relief Committee, departed from Wuchang on the "Ren'ai" gunboat on the 4th to inspect Hanchuan and returned to the province on the same ship on the 5th. According to Meng, "I departed on the 4th, in addition to the 'Ren'ai' gunboat I was on, I also brought the 'Chu De' patrol boat and the No. 5 grinding disc machine patrol boat for use in the disaster area. We arrived at Hanchuan at 3 PM that day and ascended Fulong Mountain. Looking out over the Diaowen Lake, it was still a vast expanse of water, with many villages surrounded, which was unexpected. At 8 AM on the 5th, we departed from Hanchuan and went by land to Caojia River to inspect the Yiwen Dike, the overflow of the southern and northern banks of Hugang Hunan. Although the floodwaters had receded along the way, the terrain was undulating and the mud reached our shins, making it difficult to walk. The scene after the disaster was vivid. There were about a dozen breaches in the Caojia River dike. We then took a boat to Caidian and returned to the province. The flooding in Hanchuan this year is severe. According to old farmers, it is unprecedented in seventy or eighty years, exceeding the highest previous water level by about five feet or more. According to the area measured, more than 700,000 mu of land are still submerged. Areas 4, 5, and 6 are all along the Diaohan Lake, and the fields are still flooded. The reasons are: first, the Usu port breach has not been blocked, and the water from the Xiang River continues to flow down; second, the Cao River downstream of Diaowen Lake is silted up, preventing proper drainage. The water level in the lake is more than ten feet higher than the Xiang River, causing a bottleneck, so the flooded fields will not be cultivated for the foreseeable future. An investigation of the dikes and embankments in Hanchuan County shows that there are over three hundred in total, and over two hundred of them were affected by the disaster this year. The Penggong Dike and Nanping Embankment protected the most land but were also submerged in the great flood this year. The disaster relief funds for the county are provided by the provincial Disaster Relief General Association and local fundraising. Apart from the funds used for emergency relief, there are still over 38,000 yuan available. It is proposed to use 19,000 yuan to dredge the Caojia River to address the urgent need. However, the project is quite large, and the relief funds are too little, so it is necessary for the local people to provide voluntary labor. The meager sum of 19,000 yuan can only provide food. Regarding the lives of the people in the disaster area, regardless of the past, the future relief measures are that in areas 4, 5, and 6 along Diaowen Lake, every household has a boat and can fish to make a living. The rest can be divided into a group of strong men to work at the Usu port, and those who cannot go far can be organized locally to participate in labor relief. In the areas where the water has receded, broad beans and barley have been replanted, and next spring may be able to pass safely after some adjustments. Secondly, the land survey is progressing smoothly, but recently, a quarter of the unmeasured land is still occupied by water, which has hindered registration. Previously, the people of the county registered the land themselves, with only over 530,000 mu recorded. With the implementation of the new survey, over 1.3 million mu have been measured, and it is estimated that over 500,000 mu remain unmeasured. The previous burden on the people was extremely unfair, so they welcomed the survey. If it is sorted out in the future, not only can provincial taxes be increased, but also various undertakings in the county can be gradually carried out. Regarding the issue of banning opium, the government is determined, and opium smokers must be registered, and opium dens are absolutely prohibited. According to investigators, no opium dens have been found in Hanchuan. Opium smoker registration is in progress. Caidian is an area where people from all directions gather, and several privately operated opium dens have been found. The Public Security Bureau has been ordered to arrest the criminals and send them to the county for punishment. The head of the local Public Security Bureau will also be punished for failing to enforce the ban effectively.

Jiaodong: Communist Bandits About to Be Eliminated 78

Zhan Shutang Flanks Bandits in Haiyang and Muping - Bandits Have Scattered, Clearing Operations Underway

Weicheng Correspondence: Since the many troubles in North China and the rebellion of Yin Rugeng, Hebei Province has been shrouded in gloom. Shandong Province is adjacent to Hebei, and the local security is of utmost importance. Last month, some bandits calling themselves "Autonomous Army" were found in the Daming area, attempting to riot. Han Fuju, the Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, immediately ordered Rong Guangxing, the commander of the 87th Brigade stationed in Liaocheng, to quickly resolve the issue, regardless of jurisdiction, in order to nip the rebellion in the bud. Fortunately, it was suppressed. Recently, there has been red terror on the Jiaodong Peninsula. It is said that there are more than 2,000 party members entrenched in the border area between Muping and Haiyang counties. After receiving the report, Han Fuju immediately sent Zhan Shutang, the commander of the 81st Division, to suppress them. The following is a record of the various news:

Origin of the Bandits: The bandit leader is Duan Chengzhai, who is said to be a student from a certain school. He is originally from Duanjia Village in the southern part of Muping County. Although he usually contacted bandits, his feathers were not yet full, and he did not dare to act. Recently, taking advantage of the chaos in Hebei, he decided to take a chance. He launched an uprising on the 25th of last month with only a few dozen people. Only half of them had guns, and the rest had homemade guns, spears, and broadswords. Their plan was to attack Tonghai Village, which had a local defense force stationed there, in order to seize their weapons and strengthen their forces. At noon that day, they broke into Tonghai Village. The local defense force, being outnumbered, had heard the warning in advance and fled elsewhere, fearing they could not defeat the enemy. The bandits were disappointed and set fire to the local defense force's station, looting those with some wealth in the village and inciting the poor to join them. They then went to nearby Pingji Town and other places to loot. In this battle, the local defense force of Tonghai Village did not lose any weapons, and the fire was extinguished, destroying only two or three houses. The staff of the Tonghai Village, which is a bus station, were also kidnapped and escaped the next day. Since then, the bandit forces have gradually grown, reaching one or two thousand people, entrenched in the southwestern part of Muping County, raising red flags and distributing propaganda.

Raids on Haiyang: At the beginning of this month, several hundred bandits from Muping raided Haiyang, inciting the people along the way, forcing them to join, and cutting off part of the long-distance telephone lines. Haiyang County had heard the news, and the Third District United Village Association came out to intercept them. The local militia of the county also ambushed them at Guoge Village. The bandits were a ragtag group and were quickly repelled. The militia captured one pistol and one rifle, as well as two bandits. According to the bandits, they were members of the Communist Party, ordered by their leader to launch an uprising on a scheduled date, and the party members had already united several thousand people.

Yantai Imposes Martial Law: Yantai is very close to Muping County. In order to prevent incidents, the county Public Security Bureau has issued a special order to all entertainment venues to stop business at 11:00 PM every night. The street leaders of Qishan received an order from the Second Branch Bureau to close the city gates at 10:00 PM every night and open them at 5:00 AM in the morning, and not to open them at any time. The street leaders have informed the residents to comply. The east, west, and north gates are all closed at 10:00 PM, leaving only the south gate open for traffic.

Han Orders Ruthless Suppression: After the bandits launched their incident, Li Shusen, the magistrate of Fushan County, was the first to report to the provincial government. The other counties also reported to Jinan one after another. After receiving the report, Chairman Han immediately appointed Zhan Shutang, the commander of the 81st Division in Weixian, as the Clearing Commissioner of Laiyang, Haiyang, Muping, Wendeng, and Rongcheng counties, and sent his direct troops and two infantry regiments to the counties to carry out clearing operations. He also issued clearing regulations for compliance. The intelligence fees required during the clearing period were paid by the headquarters, calculated at 200 yuan per regiment, 300 yuan per brigade, and 400 yuan per division. He also ordered that goods be purchased at a price and not requisitioned from the people. Each soldier and horse was paid four cents per day.

Clearing Conference: After receiving the order, Zhan Shutang arrived in Laiyang on the 30th and convened a clearing conference. Attendees included Zhan Shutang, Brigade Commander Tang Bangzhi, Regiment Commander Zhao Tingbi, Laiyang County Magistrate Liang Bingkun, Haiyang County Magistrate Luo Ming, Muping County Magistrate Wang Zhaoxu, Wendeng County Magistrate Liu Chongwu, and Rongcheng County Magistrate Qiu Zhongdu. It was resolved that the local militia in each county would cooperate with the military to block and actively clear the area.

Flanking Attack: According to news from Yantai, Zhan Shutang's Brigade Commander Yun Suanchang, stationed in Weixian, was ordered to lead his troops in 28 motor vehicles to Yantai. After a brief rest, they went to Muping. The troops stationed in Muping also took more than 20 motor vehicles from Muwei Rongduan and went south from Muping to pursue. At the same time, a regiment of troops was sent from Laiyang to Haiyang. Zhan Shutang himself also went to Haiyang from Laiyang. In the two-pronged attack, the bandits were reportedly defeated on the 4th, with a dozen bandits killed and more than 200 captured. The clearing operations are still continuing.

Pacification Progress in Southern Jiangxi 79

First Army Handles Winter Defense and Bandit Suppression - Xun'an Highway Being Built Quickly - Preparations Underway for Guanggan Civil Aviation

Guangzhou Correspondence: At the end of last month, the Direct Guard Regiment of the First Army and the Fifth Regiment of the Second Division, commanded by Chen Shuying, were transferred from Ganzhou to Jiangkou, located at the border of Ganxian, Xingdu, and Xingguo, and stationed there. After receiving the order, Chen's regiment arrived at Jiangkou on the 29th of last month to take up defensive positions, responsible for searching and suppressing the remaining bandits and maintaining stability in the area east of the Gan River. At the same time, the Second Division dispatched the Fourth and Sixth Regiments and the Training Regiment to advance into the Ganzhou, Dabu, and Wangmudu areas to cooperate with the Jiangkou garrison in organizing winter defense. The Xin'feng defense area, which was left behind, is temporarily being taken care of by the Third Division stationed in Anyuan, commanded by Zhang Ruigui. As for a part of the First Division, it is currently led by Commander Peng Linsheng to the border of Hunan, to suppress the remaining bandits. According to a telegram from the Deputy Commander yesterday, the First Division has been searching and suppressing local bandits in Hunan county for several days, capturing more than 20 people and seizing over 100 guns, rescuing more than a dozen kidnapped men and women. The remaining bandits are currently hiding in the Zixing area and are being tracked and suppressed. Another group of remnant bandits led by Yang Musen, after being intercepted by the 13th Battalion and the 11th and 12th Companies of the Jiangxi Border Security Force, fled into Zixing. The Jiangxi Security Force has also returned to Suichuan. It is reported that the bandit forces have recently surrendered to Deputy Commander Peng, who has telegraphed the army headquarters for instructions. In addition to searching and suppressing the remaining bandits, the two divisions of the First Army have also been paying attention to the construction of the Gan-Nan Highway. The roads in Xinfeng have been completed in succession, and the construction of the Anxun Highway is being rushed. This road runs from Anyuan to Xunwu, 180 li long, and the army headquarters has ordered the two counties of Xunwu and Anyuan to collect civilian labor in sections to build the roadbed. Recently, the Xin'feng Engineering Team leader was dispatched to Anyuan with the entire team to accelerate the work, which is scheduled to be completed by the end of this year to facilitate transportation. The Southwest Civil Aviation Company is now with Gan. In terms of transportation, although each highway has between routes is long, and round trips are required. In order to speed up the message, it is planned to set up a Gan-Guang civil aviation line in the near future. The line originally took Guangzhou and Nanchang as the main stations, and Shaozhou, Dayu, Ganxian, and Ji'an as branch stations. Later, because the establishment of a station in Nanchang needs to be discussed with the Jiangxi Provincial Government, before the agreement is reached, Ganzhou will be temporarily used as the terminal, and branch stations will be set up in Shaoguan and Dayu. A pilot and telegraph station staff have been sent to survey the route and find a suitable flying field. On the one hand, two Dingson pure machines were ordered from a certain country's company for use on this line, and they will be expanded in the future if they develop. (December 3) It was found in the Jiangzhen Special Service Team that a team flag was seized, which was in line with the secret report that Xue Juqing intercepted the brigade, Zhang said that the flag was not issued by the superiors, and it was obviously made privately by the department. On the previous day, the district department was ordered to detain Xue, and Li Jingwen fled after hearing the news, and is now being investigated.

The Dongting Xishan Chengjin Coal Mine uses local methods to mine coal, and can mine more than 20 tons per day. However, due to poor management, there are often disputes. The Shanghai Xishan Fellow Villagers Association took the workers of the mine and repeatedly petitioned the governor for the establishment of and asked for a ban, and all the merchants in the mountain that it was not in accordance with the regulations, and there were disturbances to merchants, so on the 8th, they jointly petitioned the government, demanding to stop mining, and asked the military and police to dismiss the guest workers to avoid disturbances.

Wuxi: Banning Private Prostitution and Opening Public Prostitution 81

Chen Yuchu, the director of the County Public Security Bureau, believes that Wuxi is full of private prostitutes, and the prohibition is not effective. He has repeatedly proposed methods such as setting up training centers and shelters, but due to limited funds, it is actually difficult to implement them. However, if this continues, it will harm society and the health of the family. Now it is found that Jiangsu Province has been banning for a long time, and since the trial in the provincial capital, it has been successful. The situation of prostitutes in Wuxi is different. It is not enough to solve the problem by strictly following the ban. During the 61st police affairs meeting, it was proposed for discussion, and it was decided that: (1) Following the example of Wu County, draft various regulations and submit them for approval; (2) Temporarily designate Beichengjiao and Youshanchuanbang as first-class prostitute areas, Wanxiang as second-class prostitute areas, and Dongxin Road as third-class prostitute areas. The sections will work with the competent branches to survey and deal with them.

Provincial Order to Reorganize County Business Regiments 83

The Provincial Government previously issued an order that all business regiments in the counties should be abolished by the first day of last month. The business regiments in Wuxi, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Chongming, Huaiyin, Shanghai, and other places were reorganized into militia reserve teams or sentry posts according to the county's militia training methods, and were controlled by the county magistrates and commanded by the local district chiefs and township chiefs. After receiving the order, most of the business regiments in the counties advocated that the principle of not deviating from the word "business" should be followed, so it has not been implemented yet. It is necessary to wait until after the winter defense before reorganizing. The Provincial Security Department issued another order to the county government yesterday, ordering the cancellation of the name of the business regiment as soon as possible, and reorganizing it according to the regulations as soon as possible. There shall be no other changes in name to obscure the provincial order.

Jiaxing: Resolution of Slaughter Tax Case 87

The county stipulates that the slaughter tax of fresh meat in Jiaxing will be increased by 65% of the regular tax. Each pig must pay a surcharge of two jiao and six fen. The meat merchants expressed their disagreement because they could not afford it. The county magistrate ordered the Public Security Bureau to summon and detain eleven meat merchants. Although the county chamber of commerce requested bail, it was rejected. Now it is learned that the case has been resolved after several consultations. The county government has approved the exemption of the seventh and eighth months, and the donation amount is still planned to be 65%, which must not be reduced. The meat merchants have agreed to pay, so the meat merchants who were in custody have also been released.

Hangzhou: Nantam Section to Open Next Month 89

Since the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway Nantam Section was actively built, the track-laying project has been carried out in four sections, and the entire section can be connected before and after the 15th of this month. More than a dozen bridges along the way have been completed one after another. Only the two major bridges of Liangjiadu and Guixi will be completed in about 20 days. Stealing Huge Sum of Money and Escaping to Hangzhou to Be Arrested 90

Chen Shunxiang, a telephone operator at the Shanghai An Yu Securities Exchange, is from Shangyu and is 19 years old. He stayed at a hotel in the city station. That night, the Public Security Bureau checked the room and found him suspicious.
