Ningbo: Cracking Down on Private Silver Smuggling Agencies 91

The Ningbo Public Security Bureau learned the other day that a certain party in Shanghai was secretly buying silver in Yong, and the smuggling agency was located at No. 102 Shizi Street. After receiving the report, Director Yu secretly sent staff members to disguise themselves as civilians and secretly observe the movements in the vicinity. On the morning of the 6th, they saw Ding Axiang, a waiter on the Ning Shao Wheel, carrying a package outside the house at that number. Seeing that the shape was quite heavy, the police jumped out and detained him. After inspecting the package, it was shockingly 500 yuan. When they searched the room, no silver was found. Only Qiu, the wife of Li Axing, lived there. Li Axing, the owner of the house, had already fled after hearing the news. The police then sent the captured criminals Ding Axiang and Qiu, together with the silver, to the headquarters for handling.

Nanhui: The Captain Sells Smuggled Salt, and the Salt Case Is Broken 92

The Second District Jiangzhen Tax Police Special Service Team seized a large ship of smuggled salt, about 300 dan, at Waishan Zao half a month ago. Then, the team leader Li Liangwen privately sold more than 100 dan, and only sent the remaining amount to the Shanghai Second District Department. Then, he loaded hundreds of dan of smuggled salt and transported it to Chuansha, and started the shore on Heqing Beach. He was detected by Han Jingzhou, the deputy captain of the Zhuqiao Commercial Patrol Team, and sent the team scout Ma Huangjin to detain him, and found a tax police special service team flag with the words Jiangzhen on board. After being led by the team leader Xue Juqing, he prepared a document to send the ship and salt to the Shanghai Second District Department for handling. However, Xue had a joint smuggling relationship with Li, so he did not send the team flag together. The Second District Department was secretly reported and forwarded to the Nanxiang Tax Police Bureau. Deputy Director Zhang Qingcheng arrived in Nanmi.

Songjiang: Extortion Case Solved on the Spot 93

Fei Zhang's family at No. 2272 Zhongshan Road, Dongnei, in this city, has some assets. On the evening of the 3rd, they received a threatening letter from Lin Yixi, claiming to be the leader of the San Ai Party, claiming to borrow 50 yuan, otherwise, he would use a pistol against a gun, etc. Fei's surname initially ignored it. But he received a reminder letter, instructing him to put the money in the envelope of the letter and hide it under the incense burner of Dingren Temple next door, and light incense candles as a signal. Fei Zhang's family put five yuan of silver, covered with the Fei stamp of Shuzhitang, and set it up as instructed. Another servant, Sun A'nan, was sent to reconnoiter in the vicinity. Sure enough, a young man was seen entering the hall this afternoon, taking out the envelope and hiding it in his pocket, and left happily. He was captured by the servant and sent to the Public Security First Sub-Station for questioning. However, Su Xingqing, who was a carpenter, came out to stop him, and the neighbors recognized that Su was suspected and sent him to the bureau together. After interrogation, the young man's name was Wang Yongchang, 18 years old, from Sijing, and he was apprenticing at Su's place. Because it was cold and he had no money to buy clothes, he conspired with Xu to write a letter of intimidation. Then Wang Yongchang was escorted to the county government to arrest Xu, who confessed his name as Xu Zengchang, 16 years old, from Zhangze. Wang Yongchang was actually Su Xingqing's son, and Su began to bow his head and said nothing, only saying that his son was unfilial and did not know his actions.

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

Our Country's Scientific Research Undertakings (Continued) 94

— Ding Wenjiang, Director-General of the Academia Sinica

(Speech to middle school students nationwide on November 26th)

All of these kinds of examples are too numerous to list. The above are merely a few examples casually mentioned regarding the problems the Academia Sinica has already begun to tackle.

Besides the two types of tasks mentioned above, the Academia Sinica also has many other jobs. Some of these tasks have no direct economic value, such as so-called pure physics and chemistry. Other tasks have absolutely no economic value, such as history, language, anthropology, and archaeology.

Let's first talk about so-called pure science problems. Should the nation spend a lot of money to promote research that has no direct economic value? People in various countries around the world have raised this question in the past and present. But in fact, every nation with advanced applied sciences also vigorously promotes pure science. In the United States, much pure science research is funded by industry because pure and applied science are fundamentally inseparable. There are countless examples of scientific applications that originated from so-called pure research. The entire field of engineering comes from physics and chemistry. Wireless radio and X-rays are obvious examples. In terms of geology, nothing is more useless and pure than paleontology. Recently, in the United States, the search for oil mines has required the use of paleontology to calculate the upper and lower depths of oil layers. Paleontology has transformed into a required subject for petroleum geologists. Mr. Weng Wenhao put it well: science is a whole, and there is no such thing as pure or applied. Instead of applied science, it is better to say the application of science.

Next, I want to talk about history, language, archaeology, anthropology, and so-called social sciences. Some of these are the newest sciences, such as archaeology and anthropology. Others are the oldest disciplines, which have only recently become scientific, such as history and language. Now that they have become scientific, their nature is fundamentally no different from that of the so-called natural sciences. Everything discussed above about pure science can be applied here. Moreover, in China today, people who study these disciplines have an even greater mission. The biggest reason for China's difficulty in achieving unity is that we lack a common belief. The foundation of this belief must be built on our understanding of ourselves. History and archaeology study our nation's past, while archaeology, anthropology, and other social sciences study our nation's present. Only by clearly understanding our nation's past and present can we understand ourselves. The most obvious example is history and archaeology. Many conservatives still believe in a "Golden Age" in ancient times, so they advocate maintaining old rituals, studying the classics, and restoring the past. In recent years, the Academia Sinica has excavated the old capital and tombs of the Shang Dynasty in Anyang County, Henan Province. We have obtained much material that allows us to understand the living conditions of people at that time. Their strange and cruel superstitions, their simple and naive lives, can greatly help us break the concept of a "Golden Age." For example, when an emperor died, in addition to the chariots, horses, and utensils buried with him, hundreds of people were beheaded and buried on all sides. Most of the palaces were made of rammed earth because bricks and tiles had not yet been invented. The emperor's sacrifices, hunts, and wars all depended on divination. They would dig a hole in a tortoise shell, burn it, and then look at the cracks on it to determine the auspiciousness or misfortune of the divination. If those who advocate restoring the past are correct, to what extent should we restore it? If we restore the cultural level of the Shang Dynasty, how can we live? The contributions of archaeology and history are like this, and so are the contributions of other fields. Understanding that there are no major differences between the various ethnic groups in the Far East can be proven by measurement. Understanding that various dialects are simply variations of one language. Understanding that the Republic of China is a single economic unit, unable to survive after division. Only then can the foundation of unity be built on national consciousness.

The above describes the Academia Sinica's method of implementing science. The task of guiding, coordinating, and encouraging academic research is led by the Academia Sinica's Council. The Council has a total of forty-one members. The president of the Academia Sinica and the ten directors of the institutes are ex officio members. The remaining thirty members are elected by the presidents of various national universities and then appointed by the National Government. The first Council was established in a few months of this year. Important domestic research institutions such as the Peking Research Institute, the Geological Survey of China, the Agricultural Experiment Station, the Biological Laboratory of the Science Society of China, the Jing Sheng Biological Institute of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture, the Huanghai Industrial Chemistry Research Society, and universities such as Peking, Tsinghua, Wuhan, Central, Sun Yat-sen, Zhejiang, Nankai, Union, and Yenching all have representatives elected. Therefore, the Academia Sinica's Council is an organization that represents academic research nationwide. When meetings are held, they are divided into groups according to the subjects already established by the Academia Sinica. Then, the committees of each group investigate the achievements of research institutions nationwide and the works published by scholars nationwide, to serve as a basis for future coordination and cooperation.

In fact, even before the establishment of the Council, domestic research institutions already had considerable coordination and cooperation. For example, in geology, there is the Geological Survey of China under the Ministry of Industry, the Geological Institute of the Academia Sinica, the Guangdong-Guangxi Geological Survey, the Henan Geological Survey, and the Hunan Geological Survey. In recent years, the work of these five institutions has been rationally allocated, without any duplication, and the institutions have helped each other, without regard to boundaries. For example, last year, when the Guangdong-Guangxi Geological Survey investigated the geology of Guangxi, it did not have enough staff, so the Academia Sinica sent two people to join. The Academia Sinica sent a researcher to Yunnan to investigate minerals, and the Geological Survey sent an investigator to assist him. The Hunan Geological Survey had insufficient funding, so the Central Geological Survey subsidized it with 8,000 yuan each year and sent people to help them work in Hunan. For example, in biology, the Institute of Zoology and Botany of the Academia Sinica, the Biological Laboratory of the Science Society of China, the Jing Sheng Biological Survey in Peking, and the Institute of Zoology and Botany of the Peking Research Institute have all discussed and agreed on a division of labor and cooperation. The institutions in Peking are responsible for the biological survey of northern China. The Science Society is responsible for the classification of organisms in the Yangtze River basin, while the Academia Sinica focuses on marine biology along the coast. Countries along the Pacific Ocean have a Pacific Science Association. Within the association, there is a committee for studying oceanography. Each member country has a branch. In April of this year, the Chinese branch was initiated and established by the Academia Sinica. It is divided into five groups: 1. Fisheries technology. 2. Fisheries. 3. Coral reefs. 4. Physical oceanography. 5. Marine biology. In addition to the Academia Sinica, the institutions represented by each group include the Peking Research Institute, the Science Society of China, the Jing Sheng Biological Survey, the Ministry of Industry, the Hydrographic Office of the Navy, and universities in Shandong, Xiamen, and Sun Yat-sen, the Qingdao Observatory, the Chinese Zoological Society, and aquatic product experiment stations in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. At that time, it was decided to establish marine biology research laboratories in Xiamen, Dinghai, Yantai, and Qingdao, which would be separately managed by Xiamen University, the Academia Sinica, the Peking Research Institute, Shandong University, and the Qingdao Observatory. At the same time, the Hydrographic Office of the Navy, with subsidies from the Resources Committee, the Salt Administration of the Ministry of Finance, and the Academia Sinica, advanced the measurement of detailed charts of the waterway from the Yangtze River estuary to Haizhou. The Third Fleet also lent the Dinghai warship to the Academia Sinica to conduct research on marine biology in the Shandong Peninsula and the Bohai Bay. The staff of the Academia Sinica often teach courses at various universities, but although they hold concurrent positions, they do not receive concurrent salaries. This is because all employees of the Academia Sinica are strictly restricted from receiving any salary or public funds outside the institute in any name.

In addition, there are many other projects in which the Academia Sinica cooperates with various parties, and I do not have time to explain them in detail. The few examples mentioned above can already prove that there is not much conflict or duplication among domestic research institutions. And their spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation can serve as a model for other organizations.

Finally, there is one more issue worth discussing. When I broadcasted last time, I said that the amount of money spent on scientific research annually in China, both public and private, is approximately four million yuan. To understand the meaning of this number, we can compare it with other countries. According to estimates by the National Research Council of the United States, the cost of industrial research in the United States is approximately 750,000 gold dollars per day. Therefore, the entire nation's annual expenditure on scientific research is less than the amount spent on industrial research in the United States in two days. The numbers mentioned above do not include the various museums, universities, and government institutions in the United States, such as the Central Geological Survey. The Central Geological Survey alone has an annual budget of more than three million gold dollars. Adding all items together, the United States spends at least 300 million gold dollars on scientific research each year. According to the current exchange rate, this is approximately 900 million national currency. Therefore, our expenditure on scientific research is less than two-hundredths of that of the United States. According to Huxley's estimate, the cost of scientific research in the United Kingdom is approximately one-quarter of that of the United States, which is fifty times more than ours. Our population is four times larger than that of the United States and eight times larger than that of the United Kingdom. Our industry and academics are decades behind those of the United States and the United Kingdom. From this, we can see that the expenditure we currently spend on scientific research is truly just a drop in the bucket compared to our needs. (The End)

Flooding in Hanchuan Has Not Receded 96

More Than 700,000 Mu of Fertile Land Still Submerged in Water. Cao River and Gao Xiang River, One Zhang Deep, Urgently Need Dredging

Correspondent's Dispatch. This year's flood disaster in Hubei Province was most severe in the Xiang River basin, including Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan counties. The land flooded has not receded from summer until winter, and the suffering of the disaster victims has likely exceeded historical records. Meng Guangpeng, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs and Chairman of the Disaster Relief Committee, departed from Wuchang on the Ren'ai gunboat on the 4th to inspect Hanchuan. On the 5th, he returned to the province on the same ship. According to Meng's statement, "I departed on the 4th, taking the Chude patrol boat and the No. 5 millstone machine patrol with me in addition to the Ren'ai gunboat I was on, for use in the disaster area. We arrived in Hanchuan at 3 PM that day and climbed Mount Fulong, overlooking Lake Tiaowen, which was still a vast expanse of water. Many villages were surrounded, especially in Yongzhong, which was unexpected. At 8 AM on the 5th, we departed from Hanchuan, went to Caojia River by land, and inspected the Yiwenti embankment, the overflow of the Gang Hunan and Beiyuan. Although the flood had receded along the way, the ups and downs were muddy and knee-deep, making it inconvenient to walk. The scene after the disaster was vivid in my mind. There were about dozens of breaches in the Caojia River embankment. We then took a boat to Caidian and returned to the province. The flood disaster in Hanchuan this year was severe. According to old farmers, it was unprecedented in the past 70-80 years, exceeding the previous highest water level by about five feet or more. According to the cleaned acreage, the area still submerged is over 700,000 mu. Districts 4, 5, and 6, all along Lake Tiaohan, have land still submerged. The reasons are that the breach at Jiukou has not been blocked, the water of the Xiang River is still flowing down, and the Cao River downstream of Lake Tiaowen is silted up, impeding drainage. The water level of the lake is more than one zhang higher than that of the Xiang River, causing a blockage with no way out. The submerged land has no prospect of being cultivated. A survey of the dikes and embankments in Hanchuan County shows that there are over 300 of them, large and small. Over 200 embankments were affected this year. Penggong Dike and Nanping Embankment protected more land, but they were also submerged this year. The disaster relief funds for the county, issued by the provincial Disaster Relief Headquarters and raised by the county itself, currently total more than 38,000 yuan, excluding those used for emergency relief. It is proposed to use 19,000 yuan to dredge the Caojia River to address the most urgent need. However, the project is quite large, and the relief funds are too small. It is impossible without the obligatory labor of the local people. The 19,000 yuan relief funds can only provide meals. Regarding the lives of the people in the disaster area, regardless of the past, the future relief measures are that each household in districts 4, 5, and 6 along Lake Tiaowen has a boat and can fish to make a living. The remaining strong men can be divided into a group to work at Jiukou, and those who cannot go far can be assigned to participate in work relief locally. On the land where the water has receded, broad beans and barley have been replanted. In the spring, we can consider adjusting the amount based on the surplus or deficiency, and perhaps we can get through it safely. Secondly, the land survey is progressing smoothly, but about one-fourth of the land has not been measured because it is occupied by water, which hinders registration. In the past, the land in the county was registered by the people themselves, totaling only over 530,000 mu. Now, with the implementation of the cleaned acreage, over 1,300,000 mu have been measured, and it is estimated that over 500,000 mu have not been measured. The people's burden in the past was extremely unfair, so they welcome the cleaned acreage very much. In the future, if the organization is completed, not only can the provincial tax revenue be increased, but also various undertakings in the county can be gradually carried out. Regarding the prohibition of opium, the government is determined. Opium addicts must be registered, and opium dens are absolutely prohibited. An investigation revealed that no opium dens have been found in Hanchuan. The registration of opium addicts is in progress. Caidian is an area where people from five directions gather. A few private opium dens were found. The Public Security Bureau has been ordered to arrest the criminals and send them to the county for punishment. The head of the local Public Security Bureau will also be punished for failing to enforce the prohibition.

Communist Bandits in Jiaodong Are About to Be Eliminated 97

Zhan Shutang Suppresses Bandits in the Border Area of Haiyang and Muping Counties; Bandits Have Collapsed; Cleanup Underway

Correspondent's Dispatch from Weixian. Since the troubles in North China, and Yin Rugeng's rebellion, Hebei Province has been shrouded in a cloud of gloom. This province borders Hebei, so the local security is of utmost importance. Last month, bandits of the so-called "Autonomous Army" were discovered in the Daming area, attempting to riot. Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Provincial Government, immediately ordered Rong Guangxing, commander of the 87th Brigade stationed in Liaocheng, to quickly resolve the situation, regardless of jurisdictional boundaries, to nip the rebellion in the bud. Fortunately, it was suppressed. Recently, there has been a red terror on the Jiaodong Peninsula. It is reported that more than 2,000 party members are entrenched in the border area of Muping and Haiyang counties. Upon receiving the report, Han Fuqu immediately sent Zhan Shutang, commander of the 81st Division, to suppress them. The following is a record of the news:

Origin of the Bandits: The bandit leader is Duan Chengzhai. He is said to be a student from a certain school, originally from Duanjia Village in the southern part of Muping County. Although he had contact with bandits on a regular basis, he was not powerful enough to take action. Recently, taking advantage of the unrest in Hebei, he decided to make an attempt. He launched an uprising on the 25th of last month with only a few dozen people. Only half of them had guns. The rest had homemade guns, spears, and broadswords. Their plan was to seize the guns of the local defense force stationed in Tonghai Village, as there were only a few of them, to strengthen their forces. At noon that day, they broke into Tonghai Village. Because the defense force was small in number and had received a warning beforehand, they avoided confrontation and fled elsewhere. The bandits were disappointed, so they set fire to the defense force's station and looted those in the village who had some wealth, inciting poor people to join them. They then went to nearby Pingji Town and other places to loot. In this operation, the Tonghai Village defense force did not lose any guns, and the fire in the houses was also extinguished, only destroying two or three rooms. Tonghai Village is a bus stop, and the station staff were also taken away, only to escape the next day. From then on, the bandit force gradually grew, reaching 1,000 to 2,000 people, entrenched in the southwestern part of Muping County, with reddish-brown flags and propaganda materials.

Raiding Haiyang: At the beginning of this month, several hundred bandits raided Haiyang from Muping, inciting the people along the way to join them by force, and cutting off part of the long-distance telephone line. Haiyang County had already heard the news. The Joint Village Association of the Third District came out to intercept them, and the local militia also intercepted them at Guoge Village. The bandits were a motley crowd and were quickly repulsed. The militia captured a pistol and a rifle, as well as two bandits. According to the bandits, they were communists and were ordered by their leader to launch an uprising at a fixed time. It was reported that thousands of party members had joined forces.

Martial Law in Yantai: Yantai is very close to Muping County. For the sake of prevention, the Public Security Bureau of the county issued a notice to all entertainment venues to stop business at 11 PM every night. The street chiefs of the Qishan area received a notice from the second branch bureau under their jurisdiction to close the city gates at 10 PM every night and open them at 5 AM the next morning, and not to open them at any time. The street chiefs have informed the residents to comply. The east, west, and north gates are all set to close at 10 PM, leaving only the south gate open for passage.

Han Orders a Fierce Suppression: After the bandits launched their uprising, Li Shusen, Magistrate of Fushan County, was the first to report it to the provincial government. The other counties also reported it to Jinan one after another. Upon receiving the report, Chairman Han immediately dispatched Zhan Shutang, commander of the 81st Division in Weixian, as the Clearing Commander for Laiyang, Haiyang, Muping, Wendeng, and Rongcheng counties, leading his direct troops and two infantry regiments to carry out the cleaning in the counties and issued the regulations, in order to be able to comply. The expenses required for reconnaissance during the cleaning period were all issued by headquarters, with each regiment receiving 200 yuan, each brigade receiving 200 yuan, and each division receiving 400 yuan. He also ordered that goods be purchased at a price and that no civilian vehicles or horses be requisitioned locally. The daily price was four jiao for each person and horse.

Clearing Conference: After receiving the order, Zhan Shutang led his troops to Laiyang on the 30th and convened a cleaning conference. Those present were Zhan Shutang, Brigade Commander Yong Bangzhi, Regimental Commander Zhao Tingbi, Laiyang County Magistrate Liang Bingkun, Haiyang County Magistrate Luo Mingyu, Muping County Magistrate Wang Zhaoxu, Wendeng County Magistrate Liu Chongwu, and Rongcheng County Magistrate Qiu Zhongdu. It was decided that the militia of each county would cooperate with the troops to block the bandits and actively carry out the cleaning.

Two-Sided Attack: According to news from Yantai, Yun Qichang, the brigade commander of Zhan's division stationed in Laiyang County, was ordered to lead part of the force in 28 vehicles to Yantai for a short rest, and then went to Muping. The troops stationed in Muping also traveled to the mountainous areas of Weixian, Rongcheng, and Duan in more than 20 vehicles, pursuing south from Muping. At the same time, a regiment of troops was dispatched from Laiyang to Haiyang. Zhan Shutang himself also went to Haiyang from Laiyang. In a two-pronged attack, according to what was heard on the 4th, the bandits had been resolved, with more than a dozen bandits killed and more than 300 captured. The cleaning is still ongoing.

Pacification in Southern Jiangxi Proceeding 98

The First Army Handles Winter Defense and Bandit Suppression, Xun'an Highway Being Built Urgently, Preparations Begin for Guangzhou-Ganzhou Civil Aviation

Correspondent's Dispatch from Guangzhou. Last month, the Directly Subordinate Guard Regiment and Chen Shuying's 5th Regiment of the 2nd Division of the First Army were transferred from Ganzhou to Jiangkou, on the border of Ganxian, Yudu, and Xingguo counties, to be stationed. Chen's Regiment arrived at Jiangkou on the 29th of last month to take up their position, responsible for searching and suppressing the remaining bandits and pacifying the area along the east bank of the Gan River. At the same time, the Second Division also sent the 4th and 6th Regiments and the Training Regiment to advance into the Ganzhou, Dabu, and Wangmudu areas to liaise with the Jiangkou garrison to carry out winter defense. The defense area left behind in Xinfeng is temporarily taken care of by Zhang Ruigui's 3rd Division stationed in Anyuan. As for part of the First Division, led by Peng Linsheng, Deputy Division Commander of the First Division, they have gone to the Hunan border to cooperate with the Hunan Army in suppressing the remaining bandits of Li Zongbao's department. Yesterday, Deputy Division Commander Peng Linsheng reported in a telegram from Enshun that the First Division had been searching and suppressing bandits in Guidong, Rucheng, and other counties on the Hunan border for several days, capturing more than 20 people, seizing more than 100 guns, and rescuing more than a dozen men and women taken as hostages. The remaining bandits are now hiding in Zixing, and they are being tracked down. Another group of remaining bandits, led by Yang Musen, after being blocked by the 13th Brigade and the 11th and 12th Companies of the Jiangxi Border Security Team, have fled into Zihe. The Jiangxi Security Team has also returned to Suichuan. It is now heard that Yang has recently surrendered to Deputy Division Commander Peng, and Peng has telegraphed the military headquarters for instructions. In addition to separately searching and suppressing the remaining bandits, the two divisions of the First Army have also been paying attention to the construction of the Jiangxi-Southern Highway. The roads in Xinfeng have been completed in sequence, and the construction of the Anxun Highway is now being rushed. This route runs from Anyuan to Xunwu, is 180 li long, and the military headquarters has ordered the two counties of Xunwu and Anyuan to recruit laborers in sections to build the roadbed. Recently, the head of the Xinfeng Engineering Team was sent to Anyuan with his team to speed up the work, aiming to complete the construction by the end of this year to facilitate transportation.

The Southwest Civil Aviation Company believes that Jiangxi-South and Guangdong have close relations. Although highways have been opened for transportation, the distance between Ganzhou and Guangzhou is long, and the round trip takes time. In order to facilitate communication and speed up the movement of goods, it is planned to open a Ganzhou-Guangzhou civil aviation route in the near future. This route originally had Guangzhou and Nanchang as its main stations, with Shaoguan, Dayu, Ganxian, and Ji'an as branch stations. However, because the establishment of a station in Nanchang is still pending negotiation with the Jiangxi Provincial Government, Ganzhou will be temporarily used as the terminus until an agreement is reached, with branch stations in Shaoguan and Dayu. A pilot and a radio operator have been sent along the route to survey and find a suitable airfield, and two Stinson aircraft have been ordered from a foreign company for use on this route. In the future, if it develops, it will be expanded. (December 3rd)

Songjiang: Extortion Case Solved on the Spot 99

The residence of Fei Zhang's family at No. 2272 Zhongshan Road East in this city is slightly wealthy. On the evening of the 3rd, they received a threatening letter signed by Lin Yixi, the head of the San'ai Party, demanding a loan of 50 yuan, or else they would use a gun. The Fei family initially ignored it, but then received a reminder letter, instructing them to put the money in the envelope of the letter, hide it secretly under the incense burner of the adjacent Dingren Palace, and light incense as a signal. Fei Zhang's family prepared five silver yuan, stamped with the mark of Shuzitang Fei, and proceeded as instructed. They also sent their servant Sun Aying to scout nearby. Sure enough, this afternoon, they saw a young man enter, take out the envelope, and hide it in his pocket, cheerfully setting off. The servant immediately caught him and took him to the First Police Substation for questioning. Unexpectedly, Su Xingqing, who worked as a carpenter, came out to stop them. Neighbors believed that Su was suspected and took him to the bureau as well. The young man confessed that his name was Wang Yongchang, 18 years old, from Sijing. He was an apprentice at Su's workshop and, because it was cold and he had no money to buy clothes, conspired with Xu to write a threatening letter. Wang Yongchang was then escorted to the county government to arrest Xu, who confessed his name as Xu Zengchang, 16 years old, from Zhangze. It turned out that Wang Yongchang was Su Xingqing's son, and Su finally bowed his head without a word, only claiming that his son was unfilial and that he did not know about his actions.

Nanhui: Squad Leader Sells Confiscated Contraband Salt, Case Cracked 100

The Jiangzhen Special Task Force of the Second District Tax Police, half a month ago, seized a large boat of contraband salt, approximately over 300 dan, at Waizao. Thereupon, the squad leader Li Jingwen privately sold over 100 dan. Only the remaining amount was sent to the Second District headquarters in Shanghai. Subsequently, several hundred dan of contraband salt was loaded and transported to Chuansha. Upon landing at Heqing Beach, it was detected by the deputy squad leader Han Jingzhou of the Zhuqiao Commercial Patrol. He dispatched Ma Huangjin of the patrol to detain the shipment. A flag of the Special Task Force with the words "Jiangzhen" on it was found on the boat. The team was led by Squad Leader Xue Juqing, who prepared a document and sent the boat and salt to the Second District headquarters in Shanghai for investigation. However, Xue and Li had a joint relationship in the smuggling operation. Therefore, he did not submit the task force flag along with the shipment. This was secretly reported to the Second District headquarters, which then forwarded the information to the Nanxiang Tax Police Bureau. Deputy Director Zhang Qingcheng arrived in Nanhui and secretly investigated, finding a matching task force flag within the Jiangzhen Special Task Force. It matched the flag that Xue Juqing had been secretly reported to have intercepted. Deputy Director Zhang believed that the flag had not been issued by superiors but was clearly privately made by the task force. He immediately took the flag to the bureau and instructed the district headquarters to detain Xue the day before yesterday. Upon hearing the news, Li Jingwen abandoned his post and fled. He is currently being pursued.

Suzhou: Xishan Merchants and Residents Oppose Coal Mining 101

The Chengjin Coal Mine in Xishan, Dongting, uses indigenous methods for coal extraction, yielding over twenty tons daily. However, due to mismanagement, disputes frequently arise. The Xishan Association in Shanghai, due to the repeated disturbances caused by the mine workers to the local residents, has petitioned the ministry to request its ban. All the merchants in the Xishan area have also collectively submitted a petition to the Jiangsu Provincial Government on the eighth, demanding that the mining be stopped, citing that the mine has not been issued a permit by the ministry and is disrupting commercial activities. They have also requested that military police be dispatched to the mountain to forcibly disperse the migrant workers to prevent further disturbances.

Wuxi: Banning Private Prostitution and Establishing Public Brothels 102

Chen Yuchu, the head of the County Public Security Bureau, believes that private prostitution is rampant in Xiyi and cannot be effectively prohibited. He has repeatedly considered establishing educational centers and shelters, but due to budget limitations, many practical difficulties have prevented him from realizing these plans. However, continuing in this manner will severely harm social morality and national health. It has been found that the regulations for banning prostitution in Jiangsu Province have been promulgated for a long time. Since the province has launched trial runs, there have been achievements. Wuxian has also followed suit and has had initial results. The prostitution situation in Xiyi is no different from that in Wuxian. Implementing the regulations is the only fundamental solution. This matter was brought up for discussion during the 61st police affairs meeting. The decisions made were: (1) To draft various regulations based on the Wuxian model and submit them for approval. (2) To temporarily designate Beicheng Jiao and Youshan as first-class prostitution districts, Wanxiang as a second-class prostitution district, and Dong as a third-class prostitution district, to be surveyed and designated by the department in conjunction with the relevant branch bureau.

Accelerating the Construction of the Suzhou-Wuxi Highway 103

The County Construction Bureau has been ordered to build the Suzhou-Wuxi Highway and has already begun to handle the matter in conjunction with the Wuxian Construction Bureau. The route plan charts have also been approved by the province. Concurrently, the bureau has contacted merchants to solicit investment. After contacting the Zhangjian Bureau Cheng, Jiangnan, and Xihu long-distance bus companies, the companies cited their inability to invest, and no results were achieved. Recently, the Construction Department again instructed the county government to direct the Construction Bureau to expedite the project. After receiving the order, Director Zhang decided that whether the construction of the roadbed and the acquisition of farmland should commence after all the funds have been raised requires instructions from the provincial authorities. Therefore, he specially submitted a report to the county government yesterday to be forwarded to the Construction Department for instructions.

Provincial Order to Reorganize County Merchant Corps 104

The merchant corps in various counties were previously ordered by the provincial government to be abolished uniformly by the first day of last month. The merchant corps in Wuxi, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Chongming, Huaiyin, Shanghai, and other places were to be converted into reserve militia or watch posts in accordance with the methods for training strong young men in the respective counties, under the control of the county magistrates and under the command of the district and township chiefs. After receiving the order, most of the county merchant corps advocated adhering to the "merchant" principle, and therefore, the reorganization has not yet been implemented. It must wait until after the winter defense before being reorganized. The Provincial Security Department specially ordered the county government yesterday to abolish the name of the merchant corps as soon as possible, to reorganize it according to regulations without any other nominal changes, and not to obscure the provincial order.

Zhenjiang: News Organizations Telegraph Zhou Fo Hai 105

The news of Central Committee members Zhou Fo Hai and others proposing a motion to protect legitimate public opinion at the First Plenary Session of the Central Committee has been warmly received by the national press. The Jiangsu News Society and the Journalists Association telegraphed Zhou on the eighth, stating that "The proposal submitted by you and others to the plenary session demonstrates your enthusiasm for supporting public opinion. The Jiangsu news community expresses its admiration and hopes that you will promptly urge the government to formulate measures and implement them as soon as possible."

Jiangyin: High Court Appoints Commissioner to Secretly Investigate the Accusation Case 106

President Zhu of the Jiangsu High Court, based on a lawsuit by a Cheng resident accusing trial judge Zhou Xiang of accepting bribes, dispatched judge Wu Yuheng to Cheng under the alias Hu Xiaotian. He secretly investigated for two days before going to the county government on the sixth to review the files of Huang Huian and Wang Jiajun, the secretary of the Jianji Party branch, regarding smoking. In the afternoon, he also inspected the prison. Judge Wu is also responsible for investigating judicial administration regarding Judge Zhou's resignation. The High Court will decide after Judge Wu's investigation and reply.

Nantong: Implementing Inspections to Protect Navigation 107

The Fourth District Security Command of Jiangsu Province, due to the fact that the counties within its jurisdiction are located along the river and the sea, with many harbors, making it easy for bandits to infiltrate, and the downstream of the Yangtze River is not peaceful, with merchant ships frequently being robbed, ordered the water and land military police of each county to conduct inspections of all ports and wharves within their jurisdiction.

Jiaxing: Resolution of the Slaughter Tax Case 108

The Jiaxing fresh meat industry's slaughter tax, as stipulated by the county, was increased by 65% of the regular tax. Each pig had to pay an additional tax of 2 jiao 6 fen. The meat merchants protested, saying that they could not afford it. The county magistrate ordered the Public Security Bureau to detain eleven meat merchants. Although the county Chamber of Commerce petitioned for bail, it was rejected. It is now known that the case has been resolved after several rounds of negotiations. The county government has approved the exemption of the tax for July and August, while the amount for September, October, and November must be paid. The meat merchants have agreed to pay. Therefore, the meat merchants in custody have been released.

Xiaoshan: Reorganization of the Chamber of Commerce, Appointment of Organizers 109

The terms of office of the executive and supervisory committee members of the Xiaoshan County Chamber of Commerce have long expired. Member assemblies have been called repeatedly but have failed to reach a quorum. In terms of organization, only store members have participated, and most trade associations have not been organized or registered for the record, which is legally non-compliant. It is reported that the County Party Department has now decided to appoint Zhang Wangyun, Chen Xiangfan, Chuan Bingjiong, Wang Tiaochen, and Yu Jiaming as organizing committee members, and Chen Lehuan as the instructor.

Hangzhou: The Nanyu Section to Open to Traffic Next Month 110

Since the active construction of the Nanyu section of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, the track-laying project has been carried out in four sections. It is expected that the entire section can be connected around the 15th of this month. More than ten bridges along the route have been completed one after another. Only the Liangjiadu and Guixi bridges will be completed in about 20 days. The opening ceremony will be held in Nanchang. Preparations have begun, and the date is scheduled for the 5th of next month. The insufficient funds for the construction cost approximately 2 million yuan. Zeng Yangfu continued to negotiate with Shanghai banks to borrow the funds to meet the needs of the project.

Embezzler of Large Sum of Money Flees to Hangzhou, Arrested 111

Chen Shunxiang, a telephone operator at the Shanghai Anyu Securities Exchange, a native of Shangyu, 19 years old, stole a check worth 2,300 yuan from the exchange on the 2nd of this month. He deposited 600 yuan into the Bank of Communications, 700 yuan into the Zhongnan Bank, and 700 yuan into the Savings Bank. He absconded with the remaining money and fled to Hangzhou, staying at a hotel near the train station. That night, the Public Security Bureau inspected the room. Suspecting his appearance, they searched and found deposit books and cash. He was sent to court after admitting his guilt.

Ningbo: Cracking Down on a Secret Agency Smuggling Silver 112

The Ningbo Public Security Bureau recently learned that a certain party in Shanghai was secretly buying silver in Ningbo to smuggle it out of the country. The agency was located at No. 102 Shizi Street. After receiving the report, Director Yu secretly dispatched officers, disguised as civilians, to secretly monitor the area. On the morning of the 6th, they saw Ding Axiang, a waiter at the Ning Shao ship, carrying a package out of the house. Noticing that its shape was quite heavy, the police officers jumped out and detained him. Upon inspection, the package contained 500 yuan in silver. They then searched the room but found no more silver. The only resident was Qiu, the wife of Li Axing, the owner of the house. Li Axing had already fled upon hearing the news. The police officers sent the arrested Ding Axiang and Qiu, along with the silver, to the headquarters for investigation.

Education and Broadcast Special

China's Scientific Research Undertakings (Continued) 113

— Ding Wenjiang, Secretary-General of the Academia Sinica

(Speech to secondary schools nationwide on November 26th)

All such things, there are too many to list. The above is just a random example of a few problems that the Academia Sinica has already started on.

In addition to the two tasks mentioned above, the Academia Sinica has many other jobs, some of which have no direct economic value, such as so-called pure physics and chemistry. Some are completely without economic value, such as historical languages, ethnology and archeology.

Let's talk about pure scientific issues first. Should the state spend a lot of money to promote research that has no direct economic value? In the past and present, people in all countries around the world have raised this question. But in fact, all countries with developed applied sciences are also making great efforts to promote pure science. In the United States, many pure scientific studies are paid for by industry, because there is fundamentally no way to distinguish between pure and applied. Many scientific applications originate from so-called pure research. There are too many examples to list. The entirety of engineering comes from physics and chemistry. Radio and X-rays are very obvious examples. As far as geology is concerned, nothing is more useless and pure than paleontology. Recently, because the United States is looking for oil, it has to use paleontology to calculate the upper and lower depths of the oil layers. Paleontology has been transformed into a required subject for petroleum geology scholars. Mr. Weng Wenhao put it well, science is a whole, there is no such thing as pure or applied. Rather than applied science, it is better to say the application of science.

Secondly, it is necessary to talk about history, language, archeology, ethnology and the so-called social sciences. Some of them are the newest sciences, such as archeology and ethnology; some are the oldest knowledge, and have only recently been scientific, such as history and language. Since they have been scientific, their nature is fundamentally no different from the so-called natural sciences. All the words about pure science discussed above can be cited here. And in today's China, people who study this kind of knowledge have a great mission. The biggest reason why China is not easy to unify is that we do not have a common belief. The foundation of this belief must be built on our understanding of ourselves. History and archeology are the study of our nation's past, archeology, ethnology and other social sciences are the study of our nation's present. By understanding our nation's past and present, we can understand ourselves. The most obvious example is history and archeology. Many conservatives still believe that there was a "golden age" in ancient times, so they advocate maintaining the old ethics, studying the scriptures, and restoring the old ways. In recent years, the Academia Sinica has excavated the old capital and tombs of the Shang Dynasty in Anyang County, Henan. We have obtained a lot of materials that allow us to understand the living conditions of people at that time. Their superstitious strangeness and cruelty, and the simplicity and naivety of their lives, can help us break the concept of the "golden age." For example, when an emperor died, not to mention the sacrificed chariots, horses and utensils, hundreds of people's heads had to be cut off and buried on all sides. Most of the palaces were built with boards, because bricks and tiles had not yet been invented. The emperor's sacrifices, hunting, and wars were all dictated by divination. A hole was dug in the tortoise shell, burned with fire, and then the cracks on it were used to determine the good or bad luck of the divination. If those who advocate returning to the past are right, to what extent should we return? If we return to the cultural level of the Shang Dynasty, how can we live? The contribution of archeological history is like this, and so is everything else. Understanding that there is no fundamental difference between the various ethnic groups in the Far East can be proved by measurement; understanding that various dialects are completely a variation of a single language; understanding that the Republic of China is a whole economic unit and cannot survive after division; then the foundation of unification will be built on the national consciousness.

What I have said above is the method used by the Academia Sinica to practice science. As for the task of guiding, contacting and encouraging academic research, it is presided over by the Academia Sinica's council. There are a total of forty-one members of the council. The president of the Academia Sinica and the ten directors are ex-officio members. The remaining thirty members are elected by the presidents of national universities and then appointed by the National Government. The first council was established in a few months this year. All major research institutions in China, such as the Peiping Research Institute, the Geological Survey Institute, the Agricultural Experimental Institute, the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China, the Jing Sheng Biological Survey Institute of the China Education and Culture Foundation, the Huanghai Industrial Chemistry Research Society, and the universities of Peking, Tsinghua, Wuhan, Central, Zhongshan, Zhejiang, Nankai, Union, and Yanjing all have representatives elected. Therefore, the Academia Sinica's council is an organization representing national academic research. When meetings are held, the subjects that the Academia Sinica has already established are divided into groups. Then, each committee will investigate the achievements of national research institutions and the works published by national scholars as the basis for future liaison and cooperation.

In fact, before the establishment of the council, there was already considerable contact and cooperation among domestic research institutions. For example, in geology, there are the Geological Survey Institute of the Ministry of Industry, the Geological Research Institute of the Academia Sinica, the Guangdong-Guangxi Geological Survey Institute, the Henan Geological Survey Institute, and the Hunan Geological Survey Institute. In recent years, the work of these five institutions has been rationally allocated, without the slightest overlap, and each institution helps each other without distinction. For example, last year, when the Guangdong-Guangxi Geological Survey Institute investigated the geology of Guangxi, there were not enough staff to allocate, so the Academia Sinica sent two people to join. The Academia Sinica sent a researcher to Yunnan to investigate mineral resources, and the Geological Survey Institute sent an investigator to be his assistant. The Hunan Geological Survey Institute had insufficient funds, so the Central Geological Survey Institute subsidized him with 8,000 yuan every year and sent people to help them with their work in Hunan. Another example is biology. The Zoological and Botanical Research Institute of the Academia Sinica, the Biological Research Institute of the Science Society of China, the Jing Sheng Biological Survey Institute in Peiping, and the Animal and Plant Research Institute of the Peiping Research Institute have all discussed and agreed on a division of labor and cooperation. The institutions in Peiping are responsible for the biological survey of northern China. The Science Society is responsible for the classification of organisms in the Yangtze River basin, while the Academia Sinica focuses on marine organisms along the coast. There is a Pacific Science Association of countries along the Pacific Ocean. There is a committee for the study of oceanography. Each member country has a branch. In April of this year, the Chinese branch was initiated and established by the Academia Sinica. It is divided into 1. Fishing Technology. 2. Fisheries. 3. Coral Reef. 4. Physical Oceanography. 5. Marine Biology in five groups. In addition to the Academia Sinica, the institutions represented by each group include the Peiping Research Institute, the Chinese Science Society, the Jing Sheng Biological Survey Institute, the Ministry of Industry, the Naval Department's Hydrographic Survey Bureau, Shandong, Xiamen, Zhongshan Universities, Qingdao Meteorological Observatory, Chinese Zoological Society, Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provincial Fisheries Experimental Field and other groups. At that time, it was decided to establish marine biological research laboratories in Xiamen, Dinghai, Yantai, and Qingdao, which will be managed separately by Xiamen University, the Academia Sinica, the Peiping Research Institute, Shandong University, and the Qingdao Observatory. At the same time, the Naval Department's Hydrographic Survey Bureau used the subsidies from the Resources Committee, the Salt Administration of the Ministry of Finance, and the Academia Sinica to measure the detailed charts of the waterway from the mouth of the Yangtze River to Haizhou in advance. The Third Fleet also lent the Dinghai warship to the Academia Sinica to study marine organisms in the Shandong Peninsula and the Bohai Bay. The staff of the Academia Sinica often teach at various universities, but although they work part-time, they do not receive additional salary. Because all the staff of the Academia Sinica are strictly restricted and are not allowed to receive any salary or public funds outside the institute under any name.

In addition, there are many undertakings in which the Academia Sinica cooperates with various parties, and I do not have time to explain them in detail. The few examples mentioned above can already prove that there is not much conflict or duplication among domestic research institutions. And their spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation can be a model for other groups.

Finally, there is one more issue worth discussing. The last time I broadcast, I said that China spends approximately 4 million yuan a year on scientific research from both public and private sources. To understand the significance of this number, we can compare it with other countries. According to estimates by the U.S. National Research Council, the U.S. spends approximately 750,000 gold yuan per day on industrial research. Therefore, China's annual expenditure on scientific research is not even worth the amount the U.S. spends on industrial research in two days. The numbers mentioned above do not include the various museums, universities, and government agencies in the United States, such as the Central Geological Survey Institute. The Geological Survey Institute alone has an annual budget of 3 million gold yuan. When all items are added together, the United States spends at least 300 million gold yuan on scientific research each year. According to the current exchange rate, this is approximately 900 million national currency. Therefore, our expenditure on scientific research is not even worth 2/100 of the United States. According to Huxley, the British spend about 1/4 of the United States on scientific research, which is 50 times more than us. Our population is four times that of the United States and eight times that of the United Kingdom. All of our industries and academics are 100 years behind the British and Americans. From this, we can see that the funds we are currently spending on scientific research are truly just a drop in the bucket compared to our needs. (End)

Borrowing the Red One-Yuan Notes of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Overprinting the Bank Name, Adding the "Central" Character in Four Corners, and Signing

The Central Bank, due to the insufficient supply of one-yuan legal tender, has borrowed the red one-yuan notes of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, overprinting the bank name, adding the character "央" (Central) in the four corners, and adding the bank's seal and signature. The bank is responsible for issuing these notes, which are equivalent to the previously issued one-yuan notes and are legal tender. A special announcement is issued as follows: The Central Bank's one-yuan legal tender is currently insufficient. We are borrowing the red one-yuan notes of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, overprinting our bank name, adding the character "央" in the four corners, and adding our bank's seal and signature. The bank is responsible for issuing these notes, which are equivalent to the one-yuan notes previously issued by our bank and are legal tender. This announcement is hereby made.

After Successful Provision of Funds in Sichuan Province, Shanghai-Sichuan Exchange Rates Gradually Stabilize, Shanghai 1,000 Yuan Equals Sichuan 1,035 Yuan, Sichuan Department of Finance Has Begun to Recover Exchange Certificates 121

Liu Hangchen, Director of the Sichuan Department of Finance, came to Shanghai last time to request Finance Minister and Central Bank President Kong Xiangxi to postpone the repayment of the previously borrowed 4 million yuan and to borrow an additional 1 million yuan, totaling 12 million yuan. This was to regulate Sichuan's finances and recover the inconvertible exchange certificates issued by various firms in Chongqing. (The so-called exchange certificates were issued due to a shortage of currency and were not redeemable for cash.) After Director Liu returned to Sichuan, he began implementing the recovery plan. As a result, the excessively high Shanghai-Sichuan exchange rates have gradually returned to normal after the Ministry of Finance reorganized Sichuan's local currency and the Sichuan Department of Finance decided to recover the exchange certificates. The exchange rate the day before yesterday was 1,035 Sichuan yuan per 1,000 Shanghai yuan, a significant drop from the previous peak of over 1,700 Sichuan yuan per 1,000 Shanghai yuan. It is expected that after a considerable period of time, this exchange rate will be eliminated and replaced with a limited handling fee, which will be more convenient for Shanghai and Sichuan merchants.

Korean Trade with China 123

Export and Import Amounts Consistently Rank First, Main Export Product is Red Smartweed

The New News Agency reports that the commercial relationship between Korea and China has always been close. Although its trade with China is subject to occasional ups and downs, its export and import amounts consistently rank first compared to trade with other foreign countries. A reporter from the New News Agency specially investigated and recorded the situation of Korean trade with China in recent years for the reference of those concerned with international trade.

Trade Situation in the Last Decade

In the last decade, the trade situation between Korea and China, up to the Republic of China Year 19, the trade volume was approximately 15 million to 18 million yuan. From Year 20 onwards, it gradually decreased, reaching only 4.7 million yuan in Year 21. However, in Year 22, it began to recover, reaching 10 million yuan in Year 23. Although trade with China has been subject to occasional ups and downs, its export and import amounts consistently rank first compared to trade with other foreign countries. It is expected that the trade volume may recover to its former level within the year.

Port of Entry and Exit, Incheon Ranks First

Due to geographical reasons, Incheon is the center of Korean trade with China. The trade volume of Chinese merchants accounts for 60% of the total trade volume. The next two are Busan and Zhennampo. The following is a list of the trade situation by port with China last year: Incheon exports 1.150 (unit: 1,000 yuan, same below), imports 4.004; Gyeongseong exports none, imports 32; Gunsan exports 10, imports 282; Wonsan exports none, imports 54; Cheongjin exports 22, imports 4; Unggi exports none, imports 6; Busan exports 510, imports 752; Mokpo exports 4, imports 77; Sinuiju exports 123, imports 199; Zhennampo exports 244, imports 2.239; Pyongyang exports 10, imports 14.

Main Export and Import Products

Last year, red smartweed ranked first among Korea's main export products to China, with a value of approximately 800,000 yuan. Next was seafood, approximately 400,000 yuan, apples, approximately 140,000 yuan, and various canned goods, approximately 100,000 yuan. In terms of major import products, ramie fabric ranked first, with a value of approximately 1.7 million yuan. Next was coal, approximately 1.6 million yuan, salt, approximately 1.3 million yuan, chili peppers, approximately 400,000 yuan, raw cotton, approximately 400,000 yuan, spun cotton, approximately 400,000 yuan, and iron ore, approximately 400,000 yuan.

Regulations on Departure and Return Registration for Ships, Submitted to the Customs, Joint Announcement by the Finance and Public Utilities Bureaus 125

The Finance and Public Utilities Bureaus of this city, in order to manage ships, have specially stipulated that departure and return registration must be submitted with verification of the customs book. A joint announcement is issued as follows: It has been found that ships registered in this city have previously only reported departure and return matters based on the reports of the shipowners. While many reports are honest, some are inevitably inaccurate, necessitating reform. After joint consultation between the bureaus, it has been decided that from the date of this announcement, all ships registered in this city and possessing nationality certificates issued by the Maritime Administration Bureau must present the customs book for verification when returning to Shanghai after reporting departure. (First, the ship must be presented to the relevant shipping office of this Public Utilities Bureau for verification and registration, and then presented to the relevant ship tax office of this Finance Bureau for verification and payment of taxes.) This is to ensure accuracy. This announcement is jointly issued, and all shipowners are hereby informed.

(3) The Shanghai-Guangxi Trunk Line, in the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Guangxi, has been fully completed and opened to traffic, except for a few small sections that require detours. In Hunan Province, from Chaling to Hengyang, detours can be made via Anren and Leiyang to reach Hengyang. The section from Hongqiao to Lishanpu on the Guangxi border is under active construction and will be completed soon. Therefore, it will soon be possible to travel directly by car from Shanghai to Guangxi. (4) The Beijing-Guizhou Trunk Line, from Beijing to Qimen in Anhui Province, and from Jingdezhen in Jiangxi Province, via Nanchang and Changsha to Baoqing and then to Dongkou, have been completed and opened to traffic. The section from Qimen to Jingdezhen is under construction in sections. The section west of Dongkou is difficult and costly to construct and remains to be undertaken. (5) The Beijing-Sichuan Trunk Line, the section from Pukou to Wujiang, is planned to be completed this year. The section from Wujiang via Hefei to Taihu County is open to traffic. The section from Taihu to Huangmei, Xishui, and Lijiaji in Hubei Province is partially open to traffic. The section from Lijiaji via Hankou to Yichang is open to traffic. The section west of Yichang remains to be undertaken. (6) The Beijing-Shaanxi Trunk Line, from Pukou to Hefei is the same route as the Beijing-Sichuan Trunk Line. The section from Hefei via Hengchuan in Henan Province to Xinyang is open to traffic. The section west of Xinyang is still under survey. (7) The Bian-Yue Trunk Line, from Kaifeng to Hankou, is open to traffic. From Wuchang via Daye to the Jiangxi border, except for a small section under construction, the rest is open to traffic. All sections within Jiangxi Province have been completed. Therefore, the Bian-Yue Trunk Line will soon be fully open to traffic to Shaozhou in Guangdong Province. (8) The Luo-Shao Trunk Line, all sections of this line within Hunan Province have been completed and opened to traffic. In Hubei Province, except for a small section from Menglou to Laohekou, the rest is open to traffic. In Henan Province, only the section from Luoyang to Linru is under construction.

Promote China's Foreign Trade, American Commercial Counselor Arnold Expresses His Views 129

The Daily News Agency reports that the International Trade Bureau recently published an article by American Commercial Counselor Arnold expressing his views on promoting China's foreign trade. The language is mostly pertinent, and it can serve as a reference for the development of China's trade. The following is a summary of the main points: China's foreign trade has a history of hundreds of years, but its position in the international market is still very small. Special products such as silk and tea are famous in the world, but they have recently declined. The reasons are no more than two points: (1) The custom of despising merchants. Chinese society has always valued scholars and despised merchants. This is because those who seek fame and fortune would rather study classic texts than engage in commerce. Only recently has the government begun to pay attention to the development of the country's commerce. (2) Lack of competitiveness. Products such as Chinese tea, silk, native cloth, and other handicrafts are unique in the world market, but due to a lack of competitiveness, they have gradually been encroached upon by other countries, leading to a decline. Specifically, for example, the United States discovered decades ago that using Chinese tung oil to make paint was far superior to the linseed oil originally used in the United States. They began to use Chinese tung oil, and soon tung oil became a major raw material for paint, with exports increasing sharply every year, becoming a major export commodity for foreign trade. However, because Chinese merchants sometimes took the opportunity to raise prices and adulterate inferior oil, they lost the trust of foreign merchants. Therefore, leaders of the American paint industry advised the American people to plant tung trees themselves and produce tung oil. It was decided to organize the American Tung Oil Co., Ltd. to purchase 1,200 acres of land in Gainesville, Florida, and begin planting tung trees. However, this matter will inevitably increase the consumption of Chinese tung oil when the new uses of tung oil are invented, which is beneficial to the Chinese tung oil industry. As long as Chinese tung oil improves native products and sales methods, the future is still promising. Chinese tea and tung oil are also for the same reason. Regarding fresh fruits and vegetables, methods can be found to promote and expand the domestic market. For example, South China is rich in delicious lychees, but Chinese people rarely pay attention to transporting them to Central and Northern China. Also, Fuzhou mandarin oranges are world-famous products, which can be carefully selected to become standard products and transported to major cities across the country for promotion. Vegetables can be improved in the same way as Japan. For example, soy milk is a special product invented by China, which is rich in nutrients and is very cheap. It can be promoted to become a major industry. In addition, handicrafts, porcelain, etc., can be vigorously developed in domestic and foreign markets. Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, said, "To rectify China's industry and commerce, it must be complemented by improving agriculture." He also said, "To consolidate China's national foundation, there is no other good method than to improve agriculture and promote light industry." Therefore, to improve China's foreign trade, commerce and agriculture must advance together. China is uniquely endowed by nature and is difficult to compete with in other countries around the world. However, due to the lack of economical means of transportation, the high interest rates on national debt, the inability to concentrate and unify taxation, the lack of attention to cost accounting, and the lack of perfect organization in various industries and businesses, there is no hope of prosperity. If efforts can be made to improve in the future, there is unlimited hope.

Ministry of Industry to Establish National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute in Shanghai; Organizational Regulations to Be Promulgated and Implemented by the Executive Yuan 133

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, in order to regulate the national food supply and improve rice and wheat varieties, the Ministry of Industry, based on the "Outline of National Rice and Wheat Improvement Measures" of the Executive Yuan, plans to establish a National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute in Shanghai, and will set up the Rural Revitalization Committee, the National Economic Committee, and other institutions to assist in all matters. The organizational regulations have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for promulgation and implementation. The following is a transcript: "Provisional Organizational Regulations of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute (Draft)." Article 1: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute is subordinate to the Ministry of Industry and is responsible for national rice and wheat improvement matters, and is subject to the supervision and guidance of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Supervisory Committee in accordance with the "Outline of National Rice and Wheat Improvement Measures" of the Executive Yuan. Article 2: The functions of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute are as follows: (1) To research and improve national rice and wheat varieties; (2) To promote the cultivation of excellent rice and wheat varieties in various regions; (3) To research and prevent rice and wheat diseases and pests; (4) To research and promote the improvement of irrigation systems; (5) To study the grading and marketing of rice and wheat; (6) To study and prevent the bad habit of adding water and adulterating rice and wheat; (7) To study and investigate the national rice and wheat production situation and rural systems; (8) To expand the national rice and wheat cultivated area and promote the improvement of agricultural tools in various places; (9) To guide and adjust the operations of national rice and wheat experimental institutions; (10) To train rice and wheat improvement technicians. Article 3: The work of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute should be closely linked with the Central Agricultural Experimental Institute of the Ministry of Industry. Article 4: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall establish a rice cultivation group and a wheat cultivation group to be responsible for national rice and wheat improvement matters. Article 5: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall have one director and one deputy director, both appointed by simplified procedure, who shall be responsible for the affairs of the entire institute and supervise the staff and institutions under their jurisdiction. Article 6: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall have twelve to fifteen senior technicians, two to four of whom shall be appointed by simplified procedure or recommended appointment, fourteen to eighteen technicians, and twenty-five technical assistants, all appointed by commissioning, and appointed by the director to handle technical matters under the director's orders. Article 7: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall have two group directors, concurrently held by senior technicians appointed by simplified procedure or recommended appointment, who shall be responsible for the technical affairs of each group under the orders of their superiors. Article 8: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall have six to nine clerks appointed by commissioning to handle administrative affairs, three of whom may be treated as recommended appointments, and may employ six to ten employees. Article 9: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute may employ twelve to twenty assistants to assist in technical affairs, and may recruit forty to fifty trainees. Article 10: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute may hire foreign expert consultants. Article 11: The various staff members of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute may be transferred from the Central Agricultural Experimental Institute of the Ministry of Industry to serve concurrently. Article 12: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute may open various training classes for the purpose of training technicians. Article 13: The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall establish a general rice and wheat experimental field in Nanjing, and may establish district fields in appropriate locations in various provinces, or entrust experimental work to local agricultural technical institutions originally in use. Article 14: The annual work plan and quarterly progress of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall be submitted to the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Supervisory Committee and the Ministry of Industry for approval and record. Article 15: The budget of the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute shall be reviewed and approved by the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Supervisory Committee and then submitted to the Ministry of Industry for approval and transfer. The monthly receipts and expenditures shall be reported and verified in accordance with the law, and a duplicate copy shall be sent to the National Rice and Wheat Improvement Supervisory Committee for review. Article 16: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Executive Yuan.

Ministry of Interior Explains Copyright Issues 134

According to the Guoyuan News Agency, the Ministry of Interior previously received three questions from the Commercial Press in this city regarding the interpretation of copyright of published books, and the Judicial Yuan has replied with the following interpretations: (1) The real name of the author of a work, as registered by a government agency, legal entity, or organization as the owner of the copyright, is different from a work whose name is purely the name of a government agency. The term of copyright enjoyment should be determined based on whether the author still has any interest in the work after registration. If the author has transferred the entire work to a government agency, legal entity, or organization and no longer enjoys any interest, then the copyright belongs entirely to the legal entity or organization, and the term of enjoyment should be thirty years in accordance with Article 7 of the Copyright Law. If the copyright owner still enjoys copyright benefits after the legal entity or organization registers (such as collecting royalties), then the copyright owner has not relinquished the relationship, and the term of enjoyment should be the period enjoyed by the original author in accordance with Article 4, Item 5 of the same law. (2) Since Article 3 of the Copyright Law stipulates that copyright can be transferred, if the author or their heir transfers the work to another person before obtaining copyright, unless otherwise indicated, it should naturally be regarded that the copyright obtainable on the work has also been transferred. Therefore, the remainder of the works issued after the death of the author stipulated in Article 6 of the Judicial Yuan is not limited to the author's heirs. A collector who prints ancient texts and paintings, if the acquisition of the work comes from the transfer of the author's heirs, may enjoy the copyright for the period stipulated in that article. If the printed matter is an ownerless work, then after it is approved for publication in accordance with the procedures stipulated in Article 8 of the Implementing Rules of the same law, it may be submitted for registration to enjoy copyright. As for whether the work is an original or a copy, it does not matter. (3) The term "circulating" in Article 1, Item 1 of the Implementing Rules of the Copyright Law only means that the work can actually be recognized as circulating, and it is not limited to printing and dissemination. Whether the collector of rubbings of famous steles can apply for registration according to law should be based on this standard. In addition, the Ministry of Interior believes that Article 8 of the Implementing Rules of the Copyright Law, regarding the regulations on the publication of ownerless works, if copyright protection should be granted after approval for publication and then application for registration, is doubtful, and has sent a letter to the Judicial Yuan for interpretation, stating that a work approved for publication in accordance with Article 8 of the Implementing Rules of the Copyright Law must meet the requirements of Article 1, Item several of the Copyright Law to enjoy copyright protection.
