Coal Industry Association Opposes Coal Price Increase; General Meeting Held Yesterday, Declaration Issued 137

The Coal Industry Association, in view of the fact that since the promulgation of the currency reform by the Ministry of Finance, general speculators have taken the opportunity to raise commodity prices, with Kailuan coal recently increasing in price three times in half a month, increasing by more than two yuan per ton, convened an extraordinary general meeting of members at 3 pm yesterday. Over 400 people, including Bao Zhexing, Chen Yushu, Pan Yisan, Mao Chunpu, Wang Wenzheng, Chen Weibin, and Xu Yiyong, attended. Chen Yushu and others were publicly elected as chairmen to report on the purpose of the meeting, and then the agenda was discussed: (1) Opposing exorbitant price increases, publicly electing representatives to petition and implement sanctions. It was resolved to elect 13 representatives to carry out the petition. (2) Telegramming the government, ordering all coal mines to supply coal and maintain market prices. It was resolved to pass the motion. (3) Issuing a declaration opposing the increase in coal prices. It was resolved to pass the motion. (4) Whether to accept Kailuan Coal's offer to sell 10,000 tons at a low price. It was resolved not to accept. The declaration is recorded as follows: "Since the outbreak of the September 18th and January 28th national crises, the situation has been serious and changes unpredictable. There is nothing that does not shock and frighten those who are concerned, and there is nothing that does not allow speculators to rise in rank and make a fortune. Thinking of this, what good is there in sighing? The only plan is to invigorate ourselves and strengthen our ability to cope, so that all difficulties can be overcome and all confusion can be resolved. On November 4th of this year, the Ministry of Finance promulgated the currency policy. This is a major national plan that cannot be taken lightly. However, speculators misunderstood the principles and thought that a major disaster was imminent, and competed to raise the prices of goods arbitrarily, manipulating and hoarding them by any means possible. The Ministry of Finance had already foreseen this and repeatedly issued clear orders, strictly prohibiting and severely punishing illegal merchants in accordance with the law. The Shanghai Municipal Government and the Social Affairs Bureau have also repeatedly issued instructions to strictly crack down on and arrest illegal merchants who violate the orders and punish them severely in accordance with the law. However, Kailuan Coal Mine has recently increased its price three times in half a month, with each ton of coal increasing by more than two yuan, which not only violates the law but also dares to openly hoard and manipulate prices, which is inappropriate in terms of both reason and law. In order to maintain business and stabilize market prices, the Association has not only reported to the competent authorities to petition for sanctions, but also seeks effective countermeasures based on the self-determination of its members. To clarify the great righteousness, this declaration is hereby issued."

Sixth Group Wedding to Begin Registration Today; Souvenirs to Be Changed to Bronze; Excessive Banquets to Be Prohibited 138

Registration for the sixth group wedding is scheduled to begin today (the 9th) and will end at the end of this month. The number of couples is set at 100. It is reported that in order to save resources after the implementation of the new currency system, the Social Affairs Bureau will not use silver for the souvenirs given to the new couples from this session onwards, but will instead use materials such as bronze and other metals in order to avoid wasting silver. The remaining funds may also be used to purchase bouquets and other items for the new couples. In addition, the Bureau stated that when the fifth group wedding was held, a post-event investigation by the Bureau found that while many of the wedding banquets were able to consider frugality, more than 20 of them were still slightly excessive and extravagant, which was not in line with the original intention of promoting group weddings. Therefore, from the sixth session onwards, those new couples whose wedding banquets are too extravagant will be prohibited.

More Than Three Thousand Bags of Flour Injure Eight Workers 139

Yesterday morning at around 11:00, at Fufeng Flour Mill at 126 Moganshan Road in western Shanghai, more than 3,000 bags of flour suddenly collapsed due to the excessive height of the stacked flour bags and the carelessness of the workers unloading the goods. Eight workers happened to be in the path of the collapse and were pinned down. When the incident was spotted, the supervisor immediately summoned dozens of workers from other departments to rush to carry the flour and rescue the workers one by one. However, all of them were injured. The names are listed below: Yao Shaoqing, 21 years old, two legs broken; Ren Shiqing, 34 years old, injured in the waist; Pang Shengjin, 31 years old, left leg broken; Wang Shanting, 31 years old, injured in the abdomen; Ren Zengquan, 39 years old, injured in the left leg; Ren Zengji, 40 years old, injured in the right leg bone; Zhu Shaodong, 20 years old, injured in the right leg; Zhu Fajia, 31 years old, injured in the left leg. Prostitute Solicits Travelers; Tea Room Staff Coerces and Seduces; Extorts Money, Strips Off Clothes; Traveler Unwilling, Reports to Police for Investigation 140

Ma Yunyan, a 39-year-old silk merchant from Pinghu, arrived in Shanghai by train from Nanjing on the afternoon of the 5th of this month. He arrived in Shanghai at 11:30 that night. Because it was late at night and inconvenient to knock on the door of a friend's house to ask for lodging, he went to Xinglong Inn at 41 Xixinqiao Street in the French Concession and opened room number two for one night, intending to return to Pinghu the next day. He woke up at 9:00 the next morning, feeling hungry, and asked the tea room waiter, Wen Linbao, to buy him some refreshments. The door was not closed. At that time, a prostitute surnamed someone from room number one came to the door of room number two and peeked inside through the crack in the door, and began to chat with Ma. At this moment, the tea room waiter, Wen Linbao (38 years old, from Tongzhou), returned with the refreshments and, seeing the situation, accused Ma of molesting and seducing women, extorting money from Ma, and forcing Ma to pay five yuan to compensate the prostitute for her overnight fee, otherwise he would not let the matter rest. Ma, claiming that the tea room waiter's false accusation was baseless and that he had run out of travel expenses, had no choice but to endure the insults. The group then stripped Ma of his cotton robe as compensation. Ma, unable to go outside because his long robe had been taken, pleaded bitterly, and was finally stripped of a crepe de chine trousers, which was handed over to the tea room waiter to pawn. Ma then managed to escape and, feeling insulted, reported the incident to the French police station. Detective Chen Jinshan was sent to arrest the culprits, but the gangsters had already fled. Only the tea room waiter, Wen Linbao, was apprehended, the stolen goods were retrieved, and he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. The lawyer of the police department, Gu Jixi, stated the case, saying that the defendant colluded with accomplices to extort money, and the police department still needed to investigate and arrest the accomplices, requesting an extension of the deadline. Next, the plaintiff, Ma Yunyan, testified about the situation of being beaten and extorted. When questioned, the defendant Wen Linshi denied participating in the scheme and claimed that it was the guest who had done it, that the guest had asked him to pawn the clothes, that the guest had left early in the night, and that the woman was also brought by the guest, whose name he did not know. When asked whether it was because he saw that the traveler was lonely and vulnerable and intentionally extorted money, Wen firmly denied it. After reviewing the confession, Judge Zhang Chaozuo ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing to the 11th for further investigation.

Inside Wing On Company: Diamond Ring Switched, Discovered on the Spot, Real Diamond Ring Thrown into Spittoon 141

The day before yesterday at noon, three people, Li Junmin and Li Fushan from Beiping, and Zhao Tujian from Lu, went to the jewelry department of the Wing On Company on Nanjing Road to purchase a diamond ring. A clerk, Tan Fuyao, took out three diamond rings for them to choose from. The three, Li et al., each took turns examining the rings. Considering the price too high, they returned the rings to Tan, who placed them back in the counter. At this time, Tan noticed that one of the rings, about one carat and worth 980 yuan, had been replaced with a fake. He immediately notified another colleague, Dong Zhenfu, to come and detain the three. During the capture, Zhao Tujian suddenly threw something into the spittoon. Upon inspection, it was the diamond ring that had been switched out. Subsequently, detectives arrived and took Li et al. into the Lao Zha gate police station. 104.50 yuan in banknotes were found on the three. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, prosecuted them according to Article 339 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, all three defendants denied swapping the rings with a fake. Li Fushan even claimed that his diamond ring had been replaced with a fake by the company. Judge Dai Rongduo examined the statements and adjourned the case for further investigation.

China Merchants Bureau Adopts Pulverized Coal Machine, Can Save 60% of Coal Consumption 142

According to the Shin Shih News Agency, the state-run China Merchants Bureau had previously sent personnel several times to contact the Shanghai Machinery Factory on Danyang Road in this city to order pulverized coal machines for installation in the boilers of ships, in order to save coal consumption. An agreement may be reached soon. According to sources from the factory, the pulverized coal machine is a new success. It is a new invention in China. It can not only increase the firepower in the furnace, but also save 60% of coal consumption. For example, if 10 tons of coal were originally required per month, now 4 tons are sufficient. The machine is installed next to the furnace. Coal dust (not lump coal) is poured in from the coal filling point. The machine automatically grinds the coal dust into powder, and then the coal powder is blown into the furnace for combustion by wind power. The firepower is even, and even with a large amount of coal burning, there is only a small amount of residue. The machine is equipped with a thermometer, which can freely control the strength of the firepower. It is the only coal-saving machinery for large factories and the maritime industry.

Both Railways and Tongda Company Operate Water-Land Intermodal Transport; Newly Signed Contract of Twelve Articles 143

The Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai), Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo), and Qian (Qiantang) Railways and the Tongda Yuanji Steamship Company have newly signed an intermodal transport contract. The railway and the steamship bureau have been operating intermodal transport for many years. Now, from November 21st of this year, a standard contract has been revised, and from the same day, Dahongqiao port of the steamship bureau will be added to handle intermodal transport of luggage and parcels. The articles of the new contract are summarized as follows: (1) The Jinghu, Huhangyong, and Qian Railway Bureau (hereinafter referred to as Party A) and the Tongda Yuanji Steamship Bureau (hereinafter referred to as Party B), in order to facilitate passengers, specially operate car-boat intermodal transport and sign a contract, which both parties shall abide by. (2) Party A stipulates Shanghai North Station as the intermodal station, and Party B stipulates Youpu Dahongqiao Second Port as the intermodal port. Both parties use Qingyang Port as the connecting station to handle passenger and luggage intermodal transport. The intermodal ticket prices and kilometer mileage are listed in the appendix, which is also part of this contract. (3) Intermodal tickets are valid for the day. (4) Children under four years of age are exempt from ticket prices; those between four and twelve years of age receive a half-price discount; those between twelve and twelve years of age and older are charged the full price. (5) For free baggage weight, Party A stipulates that each ticket entitles first class to 80 kilograms, second class to 60 kilograms, and third and fourth classes to 40 kilograms. Children's half-price tickets have their free weight halved according to their respective classes. Party B is the same as Party A. (6) Non-numbered joint tickets may not be combined to calculate their free baggage weight. (7) Party A stipulates that for intermodal baggage exceeding the free weight, silver is charged at 1.1 li per kilometer for every 20 kilograms or less. Fractions less than 5 cents are calculated as 5 cents, and those above 5 cents and below 1 jiao are calculated as 1 jiao. Party B charges 1 jiao of silver per 40 kilograms or less between Qingyang Port and Xupu, and 8 fen of silver per 40 kilograms or less between Qingyang Port and Dahongqiao. (11) When transferring intermodal baggage, if shortages or damage are found, the baggage handlers of both parties shall make a clear explanation and note it on the transfer document. If the loss occurs within the scope of Party A, Party A shall be responsible for compensation in accordance with the regulations. If it occurs within the scope of Party B, Party B shall be responsible for compensation in accordance with the regulations. (12) The validity period of this contract is one year, from November 21st of the 24th year to November 20th of the 25th year. If both parties agree, it may be extended. If either party wishes to cancel the contract during the validity period, it must notify the other party in writing one month in advance, and the contract can be cancelled.

Completion of Qinghu Road is Scheduled 144

The Qinghu Road from Shanghai to Qingpu County has been under construction for more than a year. The large and small bridges and culverts from Qingpu to the intersection of Hongqiao Road archway road in western Shanghai are due to the diverse routes and river crossings. There are as many as one hundred and sixty or seventy seats, and there are three large bridges, which have been completed one after another. However, the soil is soft, and now it has been replanned. A base layer of gravel is paved, and yellow sand and soil are paved on top. The road surface is added with cobblestone chips, so the project cost is very large. Therefore, the width of the road is narrow. With the efforts of a large number of road workers, it is estimated that it will not be completed this year. The opening date will be in the early spring at the earliest.

Ceylon Monk Narada Welcomes Ceylon Study Group 154

The group is currently studying Pali. Members reveal the purpose of studying abroad.

According to Datong News Agency, the Ceylon Study Group organized by the Shanghai General Buddhist Association of China has members such as Master Huisong, Fachou, Weihuan, Weizhi, Jiang'an, Weishi, and lay Buddhist Lin Hui. It is scheduled to go abroad to study at the end of January next year. The details are reported in the newspapers. Continue with the details below.

Ceylon Monk Welcomes

It is now learned that the members have gathered to live in the Buddhist Jingye Society on Hede Road to study English and Pali. The quota for the group is temporarily set at eight. The round-trip travel expenses are subsidized by the Buddhist Association and the Jingye Society. The study period is scheduled for five years. During the study period in Ceylon, food, clothing, and accommodation will be the responsibility of Master Narada, who previously came to Shanghai to preach. Master Narada recently sent a letter from Java to the Jingye Society, saying that he had sent his companion lay Buddhist Sirigua back to Ceylon first to contact the group regarding studying in Ceylon, and hoped that the Chinese Buddhist Ceylon Study Group should also prepare everything early.

Purpose of Studying Abroad

According to the spokesperson of the group, the mission and purpose of our going to Ceylon to study can be summarized as follows: (1) Buddhism was introduced to our country. In terms of time, it has a history of nearly two thousand years. Today, the doctrines of Chinese Buddhism, whether they are in line with the original Buddhism of India and maintain their original appearance, is a big question. The first mission of this group is to study the system of original Buddhism as a reference for reforming the system of Buddhism in our country. (2) The dissemination of Buddhism has two systems: Southern Transmission and Northern Transmission. Northern Transmission Buddhism is based on Sanskrit, while Southern Transmission Buddhism is based on Pali. This is recognized by Buddhist scholars. Our country's Buddhist scriptures are all translated from Sanskrit. So far, Southern Transmission Pali Buddhism has been less studied, translated, and introduced to the people of the country. Therefore, the second mission of this group is to study Pali Buddhism in order to prepare for translating all the scriptures of Southern Transmission after returning to the country in the future.

Cold Protection Measures for Water Pipes 155

The Shangban Zhabei Water and Electricity Company and the Shanghai Inland Water Company issued a notice to all users yesterday because of the severe cold weather, fearing that the water pipes would freeze. Article 11 of the company's water sales business regulations stipulates: "Every winter, users must wrap water pipes and water meters with cotton or straw as early as possible. At night, the main switch should be turned off and the water in the pipes should be drained to avoid freezing and cracking. If the water pipes or water equipment have been frozen and cracked, they should be replaced and repaired at their own expense. Otherwise, the company will still calculate the water charges according to the meter for the water consumed due to this. The company is not responsible for the maintenance of this damage to the water meter due to freezing or other causes. The repair or compensation costs shall be borne by the user. When the water meter is frozen but not damaged, the company should be notified immediately to send a craftsman to repair or replace it without any cost." Now, because the weather is getting colder, in addition to notifying all users, the two points that should be paid attention to according to the regulations are reiterated as follows: (1) Wrap broken cotton or straw around the water meter. (2) If the water meter is frozen, please report it to the company immediately. Do not use fire to melt it yourself, otherwise, if the water meter is damaged, it will be compensated at the price. This is hereby announced.

Yisheng Foreign Goods Store Tax Evasion Case: A Huge Fine Should Be Imposed in Accordance with the Regulations; The Store Now Submits a Certificate Letter from the Chamber of Commerce and Files a Lawsuit with the Court Requesting Permission to Post Bail First 157

Liu Mingjia, a Huzhou native who runs the Yisheng Foreign Goods Store at No. 54 Jixianli, Tianjin Road, was found by the Jianghai Customs to have silk worth more than 160,000 yuan that had not been subject to customs duties. The Customs cooperated with the Public Concession Police to search the store and seized one-quarter, 272 boxes, of the existing silk and handed them over to the First Special District Court for detention. Yisheng requested that the seized silk be allowed to provide a guarantee and be returned first. The court ordered that proof of the value of the seized goods be submitted before further processing. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Yisheng has sought to provide a large number of justifications, such as a certificate letter from the Chamber of Commerce, and has submitted a lawsuit to the court the day before yesterday, requesting permission to post bail. The court will hold a hearing in the next few days to investigate whether to allow bail. The customs side believes that the articles of law violated by Yisheng are Articles 21 and 22 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations. Article 21 states that those who smuggle goods in and out of the country or engage in smuggling shall be fined one to three times the value of the goods. Article 22 stipulates that a fine of two to ten times the amount of undeclared tax may be imposed, and the goods may be confiscated. Therefore, if this case is established, the amount of the fine is quite considerable. In addition, the Special First District Court had doubts about whether it had the right to hear the Pinzhen Pearl Store tax evasion case, which has the same facts as Yisheng. It has submitted a request to the Ministry of Justice Administration and the Ministries of Finance and Foreign Affairs for instructions. It has been several months now. The court has now received a reply from the Ministry ordering the Jianghai Customs and the Public Concession Bureau of Works to discuss appropriate measures and submit them to the competent authority for approval before further processing. The so-called appropriate measures refer to the right to prosecute. Therefore, the Pinzhen case is difficult to resolve at present.

A Record of a Fierce Gun Battle Between Police and Bandits in Yangjingkou Yesterday Morning: Each Side Fired More Than Ten Shots; The Bandits Eventually Escaped 159

Wu Jinfu, a resident of No. 28 Caijiazhai, Yangjing Town, Pudong, runs a cigarette and paper shop. At about 2 am yesterday morning, three bandits with mixed accents, one wearing a black short shirt and two wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants, broke into Wu's house with a pistol. At that time, Wu Jinfu and his wife, Liu, were sound asleep. Seeing the bandits arrive, Liu wanted to shout, but the bandit holding the gun held it against Wu's wife's chest, scaring her into silence. The other two bandits began to search. As a result, they robbed

5 yuan in French currency and a ring. After stealing the loot, they fled from the cigarette and paper shop and headed towards Yangjingkou. At that time, the police at Post No. 11 (about a mile from the post) had already heard the news and chased after them wildly, whistling. Inspector Zhu Yunsheng of the Yangjing Police Station heard the alarm and rushed to intercept them. The bandits fled to Yangjingkou and saw a large number of police officers chasing after them. They immediately opened fire to resist arrest. At this point, Inspector Zhu and others also opened fire, causing gun

bullets to crackle like a string of beads. Each side fired more than ten shots. At that time, the bandits saw that the situation was not good, so they jumped onto a sampan boat docked on the river bank and forced the boatman Peng Jinxiang to drive. At this time, the Pudong Water Patrol Detachment heard the gunshots and immediately sent a patrol boat to search the Huangpu River. As a result, because it was late at night, the three bandits relied on the power of the ferry boat to sail to the Pudong side, and then each went ashore and escaped without a trace. Later, the Water Patrol Team arrested and interrogated the sampan boatman Peng Jinxiang. When the bandits and police were shooting and fighting,

a stray bullet injured a passerby

named Xiao Sanzi. While walking through the area east of Sanjing, he was hit in the leg by a stray bullet. Blood flowed freely, and he fell to the ground in pain. The police station in charge then sent the injured Xiao Sanzi to a Pudong hospital for treatment.

University Student Avenges Father's Death; Friends Petition for Special Pardon; Should Be Handled by the Judicial Yuan; Special Second Court Directs Notification 160

Qian Zhaofeng, also known as Peihao, a young university student from An'nan County, Guizhou, on the evening of October 16th, in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, at 10:30 PM, inside the Huangjin Grand Theater in the French Concession, during the darkness of a film screening, stabbed to death his father's killer, He Zunfu, a fellow villager and former magistrate of An'nan County (36 years old at the time, previously serving in the Southwest military). The knife wound to the chest proved fatal, and he died the next day at Renji Hospital. At the time of the murder, Qian fled to the theater entrance but was apprehended by detectives. The murder weapon was found at the scene, taken to the police station, and handed over to the Special Second District Court, where the Legal Police Department filed a public prosecution for premeditated murder. During the trial, the Special Second Court transferred documents to the An'nan County Government of Guizhou for investigation, which confirmed that Qian's father, Qian Bin, was indeed killed by He. Consequently, leniency was granted according to the law, and Qian Zhaofeng was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment on February 20th of the following year, as previously reported. Qian Zhaofeng also abandoned his appeal, and the sentence was finalized, with him being sent to the Second Special District Prison on Masnan Road. Now, Qian Zhaofeng's relatives and friends, including Wang Xiaojingkan, considering Qian's filial piety in avenging his father's death, have jointly petitioned the Special Second Court, requesting leniency in granting Qian Zhaofeng a special pardon for his unserved sentence. The Special Second Court has issued a directive stating that matters of special pardon should be handled by the Judicial Yuan according to Article 37, Paragraph 2 of the Organization Law of the National Government of the Republic of China, and therefore, the request for this court to grant leniency for a special pardon should not be considered. This directive has been issued and the petitioners have been notified. It is heard that the petitioners, after receiving the directive, intend to petition higher authorities for a special pardon.

Two Charity Groups Cooperatively Report on Disaster Relief in Hubei 161

Continuing Emergency Relief Efforts in Yichang, Shashi, and Jiangling; Severely Cold Winter Requires Great Attention to Cotton Clothing

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association and the Red Swastika Society have jointly undertaken disaster relief efforts for the flood disaster in Hubei Province. They have successively dispatched three major relief teams to work in the disaster areas, having already conducted relief efforts in the counties of Hanchuan, Hanyang, and Zhongxiang. The progress of these efforts has been previously reported. It is now reported that the association has received further reports from Commissioners Li Tianzhen and Yu Jiashen regarding the relief situation in various locations, which are recorded as follows:

Hanchuan Area

The Hanchuan relief effort was previously overseen by Team Leader Ouyang Dulin, and it has now been completed. In the town area of Hanchuan County, 33 Bao units were affected, with 1,844 households, 5,144 adults, and 3,092 children. In the first district, which included 8 Xiang and 169 Bao units, there were 8,421 affected households, 24,742 adults, and 15,018 children. In the second district, which included 4 Xiang and 42 Bao units, there were 2,075 affected households, 6,333 adults, and 3,912 children. In the third district, which included 7 Xiang and 154 Bao units, there were 6,860 affected households, 18,081 adults, and 9,648 children. In the fourth district, which included 4 Xiang and 89 Bao units, there were 4,723 affected households, 13,104 adults, and 5,949 children. In the fifth district, which included 4 Xiang and 89 Bao units, there were 4,119 affected households, 1,327 adults, and 5,858 children. In the sixth district, which included 5 Xiang and 111 Bao units, there were 4,122 affected households, 11,354 adults, and 6,390 children. A total of 521,030 Jin of flour, broad beans, white rice, fried rice, wheat flour, Guo Ba rice crust, and fried rice flour were distributed. In addition, 138 cotton-padded jackets and trousers, and over 300 sets of lined clothing were distributed. The team has already completed its work and is returning to Nanjing.

Hanyang Area

The second and fifth districts of the county have been surveyed. The third district, which included 23 Xiang and 97 Bao units, had 4,209 households, 10,407 adults, and 1,130 children. A total of 4,209 relief tickets were issued. In the seventh district, which included 18 Xiang, the third team had previously provided relief to 12 Xiang, with the remaining 6 Xiang still requiring continued relief.

Yisha Ling Area

The disaster situation in Yichang, Shashi, and Jiangling counties is particularly severe and was originally included in the association's relief plan. Commissioners Li Tianzhen and Yu Jiashen have been jointly recommended to conduct preliminary surveys to establish standards for relief. Han Yun and Yong Cheng have also been jointly recommended to form a relief team that will depart for the aforementioned counties in the coming days to conduct emergency relief efforts.

Zhongxiang Area

The disaster area in this county is the most severely affected in Hubei Province, particularly in the first, second, sixth, and ninth districts. Relief efforts have begun in the first district, but the area is vast, and banditry is rampant in the four Xiang, making the work particularly difficult.

There is an urgent need for cotton clothing in the disaster areas of the province. The Red Swastika Society and the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association have successively transported large quantities of cotton clothing for relief. However, the disaster area is too extensive, and supplies are insufficient. In this severe winter, the disaster victims are suffering from hunger and cold, and are in dire straits. It is hoped that continued donations will be raised and transported to Hankou as soon as possible, which would be an immeasurable act of merit.

Weimei Company Exquisitely Produces Jing County Dried Tofu 167

Jing County in southern Anhui has always been known for its dried tofu. The dried tofu sold in Nanjing, Wuhu, and other places is popular because its method of production originated there. However, it has not reached its full potential. A group of individuals from Jing County believe that this dried tofu is beneficial for health and is suitable for accompanying meals, drinking wine, and enjoying tea and leisure. From the wealthy to the working class, it is a food that is indispensable for a day. However, the products of Shanghai's various tofu shops are not only unsanitary but also of poor quality. Therefore, they have pooled funds to establish the Weimei Dried Tofu Company at No. 392, Taipingfangkou, west of the Public Bus Company on Kang Naiduo Road. They have specially hired several Jing County technicians who have inherited the skills to exquisitely produce this dried tofu, in order to meet the needs of all sectors of society. It has now opened for business, and various tea and snack shops are selling its products. It produces dried tofu that surpasses those of Nanjing, Yanhutang, and other places. A Visit to the Zhanghua Woolen Textile Factory 173

— By Hu Bozhou

Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four basic necessities of life, and clothing ranks first. According to statistics, the total world population is approximately 1.6 billion. Among them, 5/8 are fully clothed, 1/8 are partially clothed, and 2/8 are naked. With the progress of modern culture, which is rapid and expansive, those who are partially clothed will soon be fully clothed, and those who are naked will soon be partially clothed. This is a natural trend. Therefore, the demand for the textile industry is increasing day by day.

Woolen yarn is different from silk, hemp, cotton, and other yarns and occupies a unique place among clothing materials. In ancient China, clothing materials were only silk and hemp. After the Tang Dynasty, cotton was also used. With the opening of sea trade in modern times, foreign merchants transported woolen fabrics into China. Woolen textiles began to appear in the Chinese market and became a new material for Chinese clothing. The origin of wool textiles in Europe dates back to ancient times. As early as 500 BC, the British Isles knew how to make clothing from wool. In the 3rd century, British woolen products were famous in Rome. In the 18th century, Watt invented the steam engine, which was first used in the fine wool factories of Lancashire, marking the beginning of the modern Industrial Revolution. As a result, the output of British woolen textiles increased sharply. At that time, the total annual export value was about 6 million pounds, and woolen textiles accounted for almost half of the total.

In the fourth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, that is, in 1878 AD, Zuo Zongtang, the Governor-General of Shaanxi and Gansu, believed that the processing and manufacturing of Gansu's wool could generate considerable profits. Therefore, he raised a capital of 200,000 yuan and established the Gansu Woolen Fabric Bureau in Changjia Lane, Lanzhou. The factory had a 240-horsepower engine and 21 looms, capable of producing 20 bolts of woolen fabric per day. This was the beginning of the woolen industry in China and the origin of our country's textile industry.

Within a year, Zuo was transferred to another position, and the Gansu Woolen Fabric Bureau was soon closed. It was not until more than 20 years later that newly established woolen textile factories began to appear in Shanghai, Beijing, Wuchang, Tianjin, and other places. The Woolen Fabric Bureau was also revived at this time. It experienced several ups and downs. Until 1934, except for the three northeastern provinces, there were still 28 woolen factories in the country, with a total capital of 3.64 million yuan and an annual output value of approximately 8.79 million yuan. Among them, 22 factories were located in Shanghai. Due to the small capital of each factory and the heavy reliance on foreign sources for raw materials, development was extremely difficult. In recent years, more and more Chinese people have adopted Western clothing, and foreign woolen textiles have poured in, reaching a huge value of 19 million customs taels per year. Revitalizing the domestic woolen textile industry to stem the outflow of wealth requires the joint efforts of patriots across the country.

In order to understand the actual situation of the woolen textile industry, the reporter recently visited the Zhanghua Woolen Textile Factory, the largest factory in the city, with the Commercial and Industrial Visit Group of this newspaper. The following is a brief description of what I saw during the visit, for the reference of readers:

The factory was built in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, covering an area of more than 30 mu. The factory buildings are spacious, with flower beds and lawns inside the gate. The layout is clean, and the lighting and air are good. It was founded in 1929 with a capital of 800,000 yuan. It employs more than 400 male and female workers. Wages are calculated by piece. Female workers can earn 3 to 7 jiao per day, and male workers can earn 5 jiao to 2 yuan per day, with an average of about 6 or 7 jiao.

After the reporter and his party arrived at the factory, Mr. Xu of the factory warmly welcomed us and led us to visit various departments. The following is a summary of the working procedures seen that day.

1. Washing and Drying Wool

Wool is covered with oil and dust, which cannot be completely removed without washing. The method is to first store a considerable amount of hot and cold water, soda ash, and soap in each water tank of the washing machine. After they are dissolved, wool is added. Through the force of the machine, the wool is repeatedly turned and stirred. The wool is moved from the front tank to the back tank. The oil and dust are removed through chemical action and machine pressing, resulting in pure wool. Then, the wool is dried by a drying machine, ready for the second step of work. There are three drying machines, which can dry 5,000 pounds of wool per day.

2. Mixing and Carding Wool

In order to make the type, color, and cost of the fabric suitable for market prices, various colored wools or other fibers are often mixed and subjected to mixing and carding. The method is to first lay a layer of one type of wool flat on the ground, add a considerable amount of oil, and then lay other wool or fibers on top of it. This process is repeated until all the wool that needs to be mixed is laid. The wool is then carded and mixed by a carding machine to prepare it for the combing machine.

3. Combing Wool

The combing process is the most important and difficult process in woolen textile manufacturing. Even a slight defect can affect the entire process. The method is to use a wire carding machine, with three units as a group. The wool passes through the first wire carding machine, where it is combed, brushed, and rolled up. Short fibers that cannot be spun into yarn are removed, resulting in a wool web. The wool web then passes through the second and third wire carding machines, where the same work is done with even finer details, resulting in strips of considerable thickness. The strips are then rolled onto wooden sticks, ready to be moved to the spinning machine.

4. Spinning

Spinning is the process of spinning the wool strips obtained from the combing process into the required count, and winding it onto a paper tube in preparation for weaving. Coarse woolen yarn, with a count of 3, is used for making carpets. Fine woolen yarn has a count of 14 to 18 or even 20.

5. Weaving

In the weaving process, the warp yarn is first subjected to the processes of winding, warping, sizing, and threading through the reed. It is then placed on the loom, where it is interwoven with the weft yarn to form a fabric with a specific structure. The factory has a total of 66 looms, manufactured in Germany and Belgium.

6. Dyeing

The dyeing process varies depending on the type of fabric. Some are dyed before spinning and weaving, some are dyed after spinning into yarn, and some are dyed after weaving into bolts of fabric. Generally, multi-colored fabrics are dyed before spinning, while single-colored fabrics are dyed after weaving into bolts.

7. Finishing

Finishing is the final process of woolen textiles. The work varies depending on the type of woolen fabric. Common processes include mending, washing, shrinking, dewatering, singeing, raising, brushing, shearing, pressing, steaming, and folding.

8. Reeling and Packaging

After the above processes, the woolen textiles have become a finished product. For the convenience of transportation, woolen yarn is reeled into skeins and packaged. Woolen fabrics must be rolled, stamped, and then wrapped before they can be packaged and sold.

The factory's working procedures are roughly as described above. Most of the raw materials used in the factory are wool from Xining and Huzhou in China. However, the breed and raising of sheep have not been studied enough, and the wool quality is relatively coarse and stiff. The amount of impurities and dust is as high as 55%, and at least 25%. Therefore, the factory has a separate wool sorting department, where skilled workers specialize in removing impurities. A small portion of the wool is purchased from Australia and Czechoslovakia for making fine fabrics.

Most of the products are sold in the Yangtze River basin, with smaller sales in North China and South China. Business conditions: Sales last year were approximately 3 million yuan. This year's sales are less than last year. At the same time, due to the dumping of foreign goods, the factory had to lower its selling prices. The current prices of various goods are almost half of what they were three years ago. Not only is there no profit, but there is also an annual deficit, making it difficult to be optimistic about the future. In addition, the shortage of working capital prevents large-scale production, which is also a reason for the lack of progress. The former is a national industrial problem that cannot be solved by one factory alone, so we will not discuss it further here. The latter requires the managers to carefully plan and find ways to improve it.

Shen Siliang Arrives in Beiping for Discussions, Decides to Participate in World Games North China Preliminary 177

North China Sports Federation Convenes Third Standing Committee Meeting, Football and Basketball Preliminary Set for January in Tianjin

The details are as follows:

Shen Siliang and Zeng Zhonglu were present as observers. Mr. Shen Siliang Will Return to Shanghai This Week

After the meeting, Shen told reporters that this participation of our country in the World Games is still the first time ever, and the results cannot be predicted. In short, it all depends on whether the sports circles of our country can work together. As for the expenses for participating in the World Games, the government has approved 170,000 yuan. The track and field preliminary election will be held in Shanghai in April next spring, and the preliminary election will be held in separate districts. Swimming and national martial arts still have to depend on the cost to determine, and basically one or two people can be selected. For race walking, two or more people will be selected. The three items still need to be discussed finally. It is planned to select one person for weightlifting. I heard that Qiaozhong has excellent results in this event and is currently looking for it. I am scheduled to return to Shanghai next week, and tomorrow morning (7th) I will accompany Ma Yuehan, Zhao Wenzao, Yuan Lijiao, and Dong Shouyi to Tianjin to attend the wedding of Mr. Zhang Jiwu and Ms. Zhang Shudi.

National Conservatory of Music Held Completion Ceremony Yesterday 185

The National Conservatory of Music was established eight years ago. The Issue of National Consumption Amidst the Clamor for Economic Construction 186

— Cheng Shanglin

I. Introduction

Recently, economic forums have been rife with debate. To summarize, there are issues concerning the emphasis on heavy industry versus agriculture in the economic construction process, currency inflation versus the devaluation of silver, trade deficits versus China's interests, and whether silver outflows are fundamentally caused by international trade deficits. Regarding the first issue, many people within the country have discussed it. I myself have repeatedly commented on it in two articles: "The Unified Economic Construction and the Rural Revitalization and National Rejuvenation," Note (1), and "An Investigation into the Causes and Countermeasures of Urban Fatigue and Rural Bankruptcy," Note (2). I will not elaborate further here. I will explain the latter three issues, (2), (3), and (4), in separate writings. Now, I specifically raise a problem for discussion: that is, the "Issue of National Consumption Amidst the Clamor for Economic Construction," as written in the title of this article.

II. Reasons for Raising the Issue

Although there are many focuses of debate in the current Chinese economic forum, one opinion is shared by the majority: that the advancement of Chinese economic construction is an urgent matter.

For example, proponents of heavy industry argue that the urgent priority for saving China is industrial construction. While proponents of agriculture argue that saving China should start with popularizing education through rural movements, they do not dare to openly raise other reasons for opposition, except to lament that national strength is temporarily insufficient to accomplish industrial science construction. Not only that, but whenever there is an opportunity to apply science, they always try their best to adopt scientific methods. Dingxian, Hebei's use of new surgical techniques for raising pigs and chickens, and the lack of electric lights in Zouping, Shandong, leading to the association of the lack of scientific talent, Note (3), is one example. Furthermore, Mr. Zhao Lanping, while not admitting that "trade deficits are the fundamental cause of silver outflows," also admits that "everything industry belonging to foreigners is China's great problem." Note (4) Mr. Gu Jigao, although believing that "trade deficits are not necessarily harmful to China," also advocates using foreign capital to build "inland industrial zones." Note (5) is another explanation for this point. In addition, amid the calls for Sino-Japanese cooperation, the Japanese side advocates developing North China, and the American economic survey team, after returning to their country, also advocates assisting China in exploiting its rich reserves. Note (6) shows that foreigners also advocate the necessity of China's material enrichment, even if their starting points may be different.

However, one thing we cannot ignore is this: does the goal of economic construction focus on the military aspect, or on the entire national economy? If, according to the views of some heavy industry advocates, the focus is on the entire national economy, then in China today, where the national economy is collapsing and purchasing power is generally weak, the sales of industrial products are a serious problem. In a situation where imported goods have long been accustomed to, whether domestically produced industrial products can compete with foreign goods is another question.

Therefore, this topic is specifically raised for discussion.

III. The Significance of the Consumption Issue

Regarding the problems to be solved during China's economic construction, there are many more than just the consumption issue. For example, there is the issue of capital or the use of foreign capital during economic construction. However, the term "capital" essentially only includes land, labor, and raw materials. However, when discussing economic construction within China, the so-called land is of course not a problem. Labor? It is true that China's education is knowledge in books, lacking specialized technical engineers. But this is only a small component of the labor force. The borrowing of foreign talent, as long as no one hinders it and, more importantly, it is employment-based and used properly, is also not a problem. As for the majority of laborers, in China today, where disasters are frequent and life hangs by a thread, it is even less of a problem. What is lacking is only the issue of the machine, a double capital regarded as a means of production, and the issue of wages when employing laborers—or the necessary living expenses. However, the issue of equipment is a problem that lies between using foreign capital and purchasing foreign goods. If a certain industry needs to be established during economic construction, it is necessary to purchase a certain machine. And the price required to purchase this machine is not something that China's financial strength can temporarily afford, then a credit arrangement is possible, and borrowing a certain amount of money from a certain country, stipulating that all must be used to purchase goods from that country, is also possible. Note (7) Bartering. Note (8) China can also suffer a little loss. As long as it is carried out under the principle of not harming China's sovereignty and being beneficial to the future of economic construction. As for wages when employing people—or the issue of labor remuneration known as necessary daily living expenses, this can be divided into two aspects. One is the guest staff aspect, and the other is the Chinese people's laborer aspect. Regarding guest staff, their employment wages and remuneration, in addition to being remitted abroad after living and consuming in China, must still be paid in cash, which is not something we need to consider. However, the borrowing of specialized personnel and guest staff is certainly a minority component, so the monthly compensation required, although higher compared to Chinese nationals, is probably not too astonishing to pay. The payment of the necessary living funds for domestic workers, in today's government-centralized silver, can of course be paid with fiat currency. However, the government only centralizes silver and does not advocate currency inflation. To maintain the credit of fiat currency, the issuance of fiat currency will ultimately have a limit that is proportional to the amount of silver reserves. If we extrapolate further, then it will involve the currency issue itself. However, the distribution of labor wages must ultimately be in the form of fiat currency equivalent to cash. This can also be considered an important issue in production and construction.

Whether the policy of devaluing silver or currency inflation can be implemented in China, and what its effects will be, is not the scope of this article to discuss. However, when economic construction is carried out in China, if the purchase of foreign machinery and the borrowing of specialized technical talent can be realized as ideally, then the necessary expenses required in the economic construction process, such as wages, or the purchase of certain domestic goods materials, (for example, the establishment of a lacquer factory requires the purchase of domestic tung oil, the establishment of a dye factory requires the purchase of Chinese gallnuts, and replacing gasoline with charcoal alcohol requires the purchase of domestic raw materials), will require a relatively considerable amount of capital turnover and maintenance. This kind of capital, to put it bluntly, is currency. In the present, it can naturally also be said to be fiat currency. But it is expressed between "raw materials" and "labor," so it occupies the name of "capital." Secondly, speaking of the distribution issue, if the goal of economic construction is focused on military industrial needs, such as the manufacture of guns, ammunition, warships, and airplanes, then it will not be distributed among the national people at all. Of course, we do not need to worry too much about the promotion of domestically produced goods. But, if it is believed that economic construction is for the sake of the entire national consumption, then whether it is light industry such as daily necessities, or heavy industry such as machinery, if the sales outlet is to find a market overseas, that seems a bit too ideal. If consumers are to be found domestically, then it is necessary to target all the national people. The significance of the so-called consumption issue originally lies in this.

IV. The Importance of the Consumption Issue

Many people divide the countries of the world into two natures: one is capitalism, and the other is socialism. The difference between capitalism and socialism lies in whether the distribution of goods is determined by currency, especially through the process of commercial transactions. Regarding socialist system doctrines, there are originally many factions, including anarchism, communism, guild socialism, etc. However, at present, on the earth today in the 20th century, the only socialist system country that can stand and support itself is Soviet Russia. Therefore, when discussing socialism, from the utilitarian viewpoint that power is truth, it is necessary to take Russia as a typical example—there is only one socialist country, so there is no way to further divide it. Regarding capitalist countries, from the point of view of the private property system, then apart from Soviet Russia, it can be said that everything in this world is like this, and China is of course no exception. However, the point that the law allows the private property system, apart from Soviet Russia, is something that China shares with other countries. But the disparity between rich and poor, the advancement and backwardness of the stage of economic development, especially the difference in the political environment, means that China cannot be compared with any of the industrialized countries, whether advanced or not. Therefore, the existence of a consumption system in Chinese society, with currency as the main body of distribution, reveals its major flaws in China itself, where the industrial revolution process has not been completed and it has become a colony of other capitalist countries. These flaws are also different from those in Europe, America, and neighboring industrialized countries. In the industrialized countries of Europe and America, the existence of the private property social system makes the rich richer and the poor poorer, forming a sharp opposition between the rich and poor classes. As a result, they cannot overcome their internal contradictions and alleviate their internal panic without finding colonies and markets abroad. China is one of their colonial targets. But China is very different. China is an environment where it is exploited as a colony. Apart from a very small number of bureaucratic compradors, the rest of the national people are entirely poor. The economic life of the whole is difficult. China's inability to support its semi-self-sufficiency is due to internal natural and man-made disasters on the one hand, and external exploitation of resources and profits on the other. Therefore, the consumption system issue in China is not only an issue of equal distribution, but also an issue of how to enrich and develop the supply of materials, and create national consumption for all. In recent years, the basis for talking about economic construction has been based on this.

Although there is nothing to divide and nothing to share, we cannot ignore the significance of the fact that China is a private property society. Therefore, in China's current stage, material poverty is real and it cannot be self-sufficient. Most people either suffer from natural disasters or are burdened by man-made disasters, and their lives are not guaranteed from morning to evening. A small number of people, because they can share the remnants of foreign exploitation of Chinese profits, can use foreign goods to satisfy their worldly extravagance. Therefore, in Chinese society, there is actually a sharp opposition between a small number of bureaucratic compradors and the vast majority of poor people. Therefore, when economic construction is implemented, the domestically produced industrial products are already a problem because a small number of rich people are accustomed to using foreign goods, and what method do the majority of poor people use to consume and distribute domestically produced goods because they are plagued by natural and man-made disasters? This is the need for disaster relief, not the need for replenishment with cash. What method do they use to consume and distribute domestically produced goods? Otherwise, if it is the need for replenishment with cash, it means there is money but no goods, then a large number of foreign goods entering is simply eating without plowing, clothing without weaving, and gaining without labor. Why bother talking about economic regeneration and economic construction? Because in the 20th century, where currency is the main body of exchange in the world, China, which has been exploited and invaded for six or seven decades, not only lacks materials, but also suffers from financial panic. The importance of the consumption issue amid the calls for economic construction can be imagined from this point, because China is now in a time of national economic hardship and extremely weak purchasing power.

V. Fundamental Transformation or Unilateral Improvement?

Many people who study economics can understand that China now not only lacks materials, but also suffers from financial depletion. Therefore, they advocate developing China's production as a way to supplement material supplies, make up for trade deficits, and restore prosperity to the market. However, they still cannot abandon a wrong preconceived idea in this imagination. What is this wrong preconceived idea? It is that as long as production is developed, it can save China from poverty, thaw the situation of financial freeze, and stop international trade deficits. But they do not understand that developing production can enrich material life is a theoretical logic. If products cannot be universally distributed among all national consumers, then the situation of financial freeze will still not be thawed, and the plan to enrich the entire national life will still not be realized, which is a practical necessity. According to the idealists' view, China is backward in production, and as long as production is developed, China can be promoted to a successful modern road. Then, all established Chinese-led enterprises can operate prosperously, and there should be no risk of business depression or bankruptcy. However, this is not the case. As long as you open the daily and monthly publications, you will know that China's industry is getting worse and worse, and bankruptcy and shutdowns are seen every few days. Why is this? The influence of foreign commodity dumping policies is certainly the biggest reason. However, the fact that domestic industrial production is for business and profit is also a reason. If it can be rationally and universally distributed among all national people for consumption, then even if the foreign commodity dumping policy is more intense, in fact, the prosperity of China's industry can still be expected soon. Try to comprehensively statistically analyze the annual imports of foreign goods and the amount of China's own production, and then make a consumption comparison of the population figures, and you will know that what I said is not false.

Naturally, what I said is not that no one has noticed. In recent years, the call to revitalize rural areas and the implementation of bank investment in rural areas, although motivated by the lack of outlets for funds, (Note 9), and political factors, (Note 10), the significance of restoring the general national purchasing power and stimulating industrial and commercial prosperity is consistent. Unfortunately, this superficial relief cannot have a fundamental effect. The reasons are:

(1) The national trauma is too deep, and unilateral relief is ultimately a drop in the bucket, with no real effect.

(2) Natural and man-made disasters, especially the communist floods, further expand the extent of people's displacement and bankruptcy, making it feel that the relief is not enough.

(3) The government only talks about revitalizing rural areas, only seeing empty words. Banks implement investment in rural areas for business purposes, not for relief purposes, so there are restrictions, and it cannot be popularized to the vast majority of people in extreme poverty.

(4) In today's society where commercial transactions are the main body of consumption and distribution, domestic goods are difficult to compete with foreign goods, and domestic goods factories are difficult to compete with foreign factories, (Note 11). As a result, even if the people's purchasing power can be restored, it will only consume more foreign goods, causing silver to flow out even more. Moreover, economic construction is a slow process, and until now, only calls have been heard, and it has not been implemented in practice.

Of these four reasons, apart from the last one, which is temporarily put aside, the other three reasons are enough to explain that the consumption issue of economic construction cannot be effective in today's commercial distribution system. At this point, some people have taken a bolder step and proposed methods such as commodity certificate systems and village-owned land systems. Regarding the merits and demerits of commodity certificates and village-owned land, and what the results of implementation under China's actual environment would be, are not the scope of this article. Now, let's compare this distribution method with the consumption issue of economic construction in terms of its general meaning, and see what its merits and demerits are.

Yes, due to the import of Western cultural ideas and theories, many people like to pursue the more ideal and vague dream of "each according to their ability, each according to their need." However, putting aside all political factions for the moment, from an economic point of view, the factor of material poverty is the greatest obstacle to the realization of the "ideal world."

Although, due to the poverty of China's entire national economic life, the doctrine of socialism, or persuasion of other countries' people, is more likely to arouse interest, that is true. But arousing interest is one thing, whether it can be implemented in practice is another thing. Do not be concerned about the colonial environment of China and the era when Russia changed the national system during the intense European war. However, when Russia implemented the initial era of military communism, the suffering of its people's lives and the poverty of material supplies are probably not forgotten by those who are concerned about world affairs. May I ask, how can the system of each according to their ability and each according to their need be realized in the current stage of China, when economic construction has not even begun? So, it is impossible for China to achieve the socialization of distribution at the present time. That means the commercial transaction distribution system still has a reason for its existence. Understanding this point, we will have the following thoughts on the method of village-owned land and commodity certificates.

1: The production method that proceeds according to the principle of economic construction to enrich material equipment should be collective farms, scientific electrical methods of cultivation. The method of distributing village-owned land or those who cultivate have their fields, from a consumption point of view, may be able to suppress the opposition of the landlord and tenant classes if handled well, but it does not help the country develop production and enrich scientific equipment.

2: It is not known whether the commodity certificate system is distributed according to consumption standards or labor capacity standards. If it is due to the former, putting aside the currency issue and distributing commodity certificates according to each person's consumption capacity, then the ideal world has simply been realized. At the very least, it can be said that the government has become a disaster relief agency. Some disabled, sick, elderly, and weak people who have no opportunity to work or are unwilling to work do not have to worry about life. The government's power is probably not able to do this! If it is due to the latter, then whether everyone has the opportunity and skills to work apart from the elderly, weak, and disabled is probably still a question! If it is at the time of being young, strong, skilled, and willing to work, but there is no opportunity to work, then the difficulty of obtaining commodity certificates is probably the same as the economic plight of the unemployed now. That being said, apart from the two points of easing the panic of cash shortages and restricting the national people from using domestic goods, the issuance of commodity certificates does not help the entire national consumption method much.

It can be seen that a one-sided relief strategy that can be universal among all the national people in the consumption system does not exist. A fundamental reform strategy is also difficult to implement.

VI. State Capitalism or State Socialism?

Regarding economic construction, there is another meaning that we cannot ignore. That is, is the purpose of economic construction to enrich national power or to enrich national life? Originally, the state and the people are related. If the people's lives are difficult, it is not seen that the state can enrich its strength. If national strength is weak, the people's lives are bound to be restricted. However, this issue is not so simple in China, especially in the 20th century. The national economy is bankrupt, and national strength is also weakened as a result, which is the reality. But if national strength is strong, the national economy will also be abundant. This seems to have only a relative reason and no absolute basis. For example, I don't need to give examples, and it is not convenient to give examples. But is China's economic construction ultimately intended for national wealth and strength, or for the people's actual lives? If it is due to the former, then the intelligent will know the feelings after reading the news that the military industry in Germany and Italy, which lack colonies, is prosperous, but the people's lives cannot be enriched. Not to mention building shipyards and airplane manufacturing plants, etc. Even the construction of roads in some provinces in the country has exhausted a lot of effort, to the point of increasing the government's task of relieving people's economic bankruptcy, then it can be known that the development of purely military industry is not only without this power for a while, but also the government is unwilling to do so. If it is due to the latter, then the difficulty of solving the consumption issue and the temporary difficulty of implementing a universal social distribution system - especially the implementation of foreign goods' price reduction dumping policy, which restricts the commercial distribution method of currency purchases (the restoration of national purchasing power is only to promote more foreign goods. The fact that the annual import of foreign rice reaches an average of 16,364,167 dan, and that some rural rice cannot be sold, is enough to explain this point). In this way, the road that China's economic construction takes, from the point of distribution, the road of capitalism cannot be taken, and the road of socialism cannot be taken either.

China, a semi-colonial country, should also open up new paths outside of capitalism and socialism.

VII. Conclusion: Control or Cooperation?

The difficulty of solving the distribution method in China has been briefly explained in the previous paragraphs. However, the difficulty of solving the consumption distribution issue is one thing, and the urgent need for economic construction is another thing. China's current situation is that everything is advancing under the situation of taking one step forward and two steps back. The advancement of economic construction is of course no exception. Understanding this point, the initial economic construction is actually the most difficult and painful undertaking. Some enterprises, whether state-owned or commercially operated, will inevitably suffer losses on the produced goods when they are founded, and even have no market outlet. If this point can be noted and recognized, and even more so, with the determination to sacrifice and continue to fight with indomitable courage, then after several years, the fruit of victory can be seen. The problem is only whether the government and social figures have this determination and power to sacrifice in the process of economic construction. Otherwise, if the beautiful name of economic construction is used to pursue commodity profits, then the difficulty of supporting domestic goods factories now is enough to show that economic construction is a road that does not work.

However, economic construction, for the purpose of increasing the wealth of the state or the people, and pursuing profits, is actually inevitable under the commercial-dominated exchange distribution system. If the state or the people realize that economic construction is bound to suffer losses or fail, then no one will carry it out at all, so how can the stalemate of economic panic be broken? Therefore, the problem will turn to control or cooperation, the significance of which is to find ways to reduce the degree of loss and the crisis of goods being stranded. On the other hand, the state can, under this situation, not formally take the road of socialism, nor take the road of capitalism. (In fact, there is no ability to take these two roads at all.) And distribute the seemingly surplus goods to all the toiling masses, and transfer the "labor" that all or most of the unemployed toiling masses have nowhere to sell to heavy industrial economic construction, military industrial construction, and national defense industrial construction. It can solve the difficulty of the distribution and consumption method, so that the goods of the initial light industry will not be stranded, and heavy industry can proceed. It is beneficial to both the state and the people. And in terms of the consumption issue, the commodity promotion issue, and the heavy industry construction issue, it is beneficial to all three parties. Here, the prohibition of "private merchants," or the shrinking of the scope of power, and the politicization of the business nature - especially the issuance of commodity certificates or similar certificates to replace "cash" - are all practically necessary. However, whether today's international environment in China can be handled in this way is actually a problem in the present situation of open doors and the presence of many concessions. And whether the morality, personality, and ability of Chinese officials can overcome this task is another problem. Therefore, this method can only start from a small place and be tried out in rural or remote areas.

In terms of form, it is better to use cooperation than control, because control only has the government solely responsible, while cooperation requires the participation of the people. When I say this, I think back to the issue of planned economy.

In short, the solution to the consumption distribution issue depends on the joint efforts of the government and the people. As for the abolition of internal strife, the maintenance of long-term peace and order, especially the popularization and rapid effectiveness of disaster relief policies, these are still the prerequisites for the advancement of economic construction and the solution of the consumption distribution issue.

Finally, I have one more opinion to explain. That is, economic construction should be collectivized and communalized. Except for the state, no one is allowed to monopolize the production organs and social groups. The implementation of the distribution system should be individualized and universalized. Including government personnel, no one's material supply distribution can be excessively skewed and there can be no facts of unfair consumption. However, this is even more difficult in China. Understanding this, the implementation of government control policies with public means of production and average consumption methods is necessary, but it is too early to say so now.

Preliminary Examination Begins Yesterday; Specialized Subjects Examined Today 187

Over a Thousand Students Taking the Exam; Strict Supervision and Good Order

The preliminary examination for unregistered and closed specialized schools and above, organized by the Municipal Education Bureau, began yesterday. The examination was held at three venues: Minli, Jingye, and Wuben. Over a thousand students took the exam. The Municipal Education Bureau dispatched chief examiners and supervisors to each venue. Supervision was strict, and the order in the examination halls was good. In the morning, the subjects tested were Chinese and foreign languages, and in the afternoon, the subjects tested were Party Principles, Social Sciences, and Natural Sciences. Today and tomorrow will be for specialized subjects. Law and political science students will be tested at Jingye Middle School, while students from other departments will be tested at Wuben Girls' Middle School. From 8:00 AM to 5:10 PM, students in the first and second years of each department will take three subjects, while students in the third year must take four subjects, and students in the fourth year must take five subjects to complete the examination. It is expected that all examinations will be completed by tomorrow.

List and Photos of Primary and Secondary School Students Taking the Graduation Examination to Be Submitted to the Bureau by a Deadline 188

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a public notice urging the submission of lists of graduating students from middle schools, normal schools, and physical education normal schools who will be participating in the graduation examination. According to the Bureau's announcement of the school calendar for primary and secondary schools for the 24th year of the Republic, "On November 8th (Friday), middle schools and primary schools will begin submitting lists of graduating students. Middle schools should also submit the students' academic records from previous years in accordance with Article 11 of the revised middle school regulations, Article 14 of the revised normal school regulations, and Article 17 of the revised vocational school regulations (students participating in the graduation examination must attach photographs). The deadline is approaching, and only a few schools have submitted their reports on time, which is hindering the Bureau's review. A final extension of one week is granted, from the 9th to the 14th of this month. All middle schools, normal schools, normal departments, and physical education normal schools in the city that have graduating students should immediately follow the prescribed procedures and promptly submit their lists and photos. If the extended deadline is missed again, it will be considered that there are no graduating students, and no supplementary listings will be made. Please do not delay and cause self-harm. In addition, students who failed one or two subjects in the previous graduation examination and need to take remedial courses, as well as students who failed three or more subjects and need to repeat a grade, should be listed separately and submit two photos to participate in this year's graduation examination and make up for the failed subjects." This announcement is hereby made public for compliance.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (118) 191

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Nan was disappointed, so she gave up the matter and shouted angrily, "Go away! You old bad thing;" So the poor ewe went alone, gently venting a complaint from her throat, indicating her fright and slight resentment.

"Everyone can take a sip, then we should go for a walk. If we don't walk, we'll fall asleep; lost people can't sleep. Don't you remember the interesting story of how Lee Hana died because she was sleepy under the snow?"

"But there's no snow here, and it's warm," said Robb, who did not have Nan's active imagination.

"It doesn't matter, we'll just peek around for a while; if no one comes again, we can hide in the bushes, like the brothers of "Tom Thumb" in fairy tales."

However, they could not walk for long, because Robb was already drowsy and unable to continue walking, and often fell to the ground, so Nan really couldn't stand it, and regretted it so much.

So she said, "If you fall again, I'm going to shake you hard," but as she said this, she gently picked up the poor little man, because Nan was like a barking dog, not necessarily going to bite.

Securities: The Bond Market Still Fluctuating Over the Week 194

——Resulting in a Gain of Several Cents to One Yuan——

Last week, from December 2nd to 7th, the market situation on the China Merchants Securities Exchange fluctuated quite erratically, not as directly up and down as before. The repeated price increases by the previous bullish companies have all collapsed on their own. After absorbing excessive amounts, they all feel satisfied, and the followers know that they cannot rely on it anymore, so they have also emerged one after another. Among them, the Jin Gang and a few major players sold the most and the most fiercely. This is the general situation of the market gradually turning from frenzy to moderation. The environmental situation seems to be slightly eased compared to the previous tension. The key now is whether the legal currency can circulate throughout the country, and whether the silver in the provinces can be concentrated in the government. When the bond market is in such an extremely turbulent time, it was fortunate to rely on the support of the long side before, but now the heat is gradually receding, going back and forth, so its turbulent situation is still not easy to calm down. The total number of transactions on the exchange is still around 100 million yuan, and it is especially difficult to make the bond market suddenly quiet due to the relationship between the two year-ends and the bank closing. Looking back on the past week, He's trip to the north on Monday, the bank still had a small amount of pull-up, and the Jin Gang had already emerged, and the market price rose from several cents to one yuan and a half. On Tuesday, He stopped in Baoding, the big players stopped pulling up, the North Gang and the Jin Gang continued to emerge, and the market price gradually turned, slightly chaotic, with highs and lows alternating, and the rise and fall were still seven or eight cents. On Wednesday, although He had arrived in Ping, the rumors of the five provinces did not stop, and the circulation of the legal currency raised another problem, and the big players gradually emerged, and the market price fell from a small number of cents to one yuan. On Thursday, the North China incident was still brewing, there were many rumors, and the North Gang's selling was strong again, slightly lower from one or two cents to six or seven cents. On Friday, No. 4 sold a huge amount, and various gangs also sold one after another, and No. 43, 46 and 54, etc., all bought in, and the market price returned to chaos, with highs and lows alternating, about three or four cents.
